Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
Case Study: The Ruling on Wife's Apostasy and the Use of Nawadir
Explains the principle of choosing narrations closest to hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on wife's apostasy (Zahir al-Riwayah, Nawadir, and Samarqandi) and identify which is relied upon today according to the author, with justification.

Core Idea
On wife's apostasy, the Hanafi school has three positions, and the operative fatwa today may be the Samarqandi view that marriage does not dissolve, due to practical necessity.

This lesson explores a concrete example of the principle from Lesson 1: the ruling on a wife who apostatizes. The passage presents three different Hanafi positions, showing how scholars weighed hadith evidence, practical realities, and the weakness of the Muslim community to arrive at the most suitable fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
List the three distinct rulings mentioned in the passage: Zahir al-Riwayah, Nawadir, and the view of Samarqandi and Bukhara scholars.
Each has a different outcome for the marriage.
2
Understand the ruling of each
Describe what each position prescribes: forced to Islam, enslaved, marriage not dissolved.
The Nawadir ruling involves enslavement and repurchase.
3
Analyze the reasoning
Why did scholars move from one position to another? Consider practical factors like frequent apostasy and Muslim inability to implement.
The author's father noted lack of Muslim power.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Identify which position the author's father said is the only feasible option today and why.
He adopted the Samarqandi view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صحيح البخارى إنه يُختار من روايات الإمام أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى ما كان أقرب إلى الحديث، سواء كان من الروايات النادرة أو غير المشهورة عنه. (۱) وقال ابن عابدین رحمه الله تعالى: "ماكان من المسائل في الكتب التي رويت عن محمد بن الحسن رواية ظاهرةً يُفتى به، وإن لم يُصرحوا بتصحيحه، نعم! لو صححوارواية أخرى من غير كتب ظاهر الرواية يُتبع ما صححوه. " ثم نقل ذلك عن الطَّرَسُوْسِى رحمه الله تعالى. ومما أفتوا به برواية النوادر مسئلةُ ارتداد الزوجة، وكان الحكم على ظاهر الرواية أن تُجبر على الإسلام وعلى نكاح جديد بزوجها.
ورواية النوادر أنّها تُسترقُ فى دار الإسلام، وتكون فيئاً للمسلمين فيشتريها الزوج من الإمام أو يصرفها إليه لوكان مصرفاً. فأفتى كثير من المشايخ بهذه الرواية وقالوا: "من تصفّح أحوال نساء زماننا وما يقع منهن من موجبات الردّة مكرّراً فى كل يوم، لم يتوقف فى الإفتاء برواية النوادر (ولكن ذكر والدي رحمه الله تعالى أنه لا يمكن العمل اليوم بظاهر الرواية ولا برواية النوادر، لعدم قوّة المسلمين على العمل بذلك، فلا سبيل إلا إلى القول بما أفتى به مشايخ سمرقند و بخارا من أن النكاح لا ينفسخ بردّتها. (۳) وكذلك أفتوا برواية النوادر فى نذر اللجاج، وهو النذر المعلق على أمرٍ يُريد الناذر الاجتناب منه، مثل أن يقول: إن شربت الخمر فعلى صوم شهر. وظاهر الرواية فيه أنّه إن شرب الخمرَ وجب عليه الوفاء لاغير، ورواية النوادر أنه يُخيّر بين الوفاء بالنذر والكفّارة، وهو مذهب الشافعي ومحمد رحمهما الله تعالى، وذكر ابن الهمام أنه مروى في النوادر وأنه مختار المحققين ) وعليه مشى أصحاب المتون. (4)
وكذلك حكوا ظاهر الرّواية أنّه يُشترط المصر لنفاذ قضاء القاضي. ورواية النوادر أنه ليس بشرط، ثمّ أفتوا برواية النوادر، كما حكاه ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى عن البزازيّة .
The author of Sahih al-Bukhari stated that he selects from the narrations of Imam Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, what is closest to hadith, whether it is from the rare narrations (nawadir) or the less famous ones. (1) Ibn Abidin, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'Whatever rulings are in the books narrated from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan as a manifest narration (zahir al-riwayah) are given fatwa by, even if they did not explicitly declare it as correct. Yes, if they declared another narration correct from other than the manifest books, what they declared correct is followed.' Then he transmitted that from al-Tarasusi, may Allah have mercy on him. Among the things they gave fatwa by the nawadir narration is the issue of the wife's apostasy. The ruling according to the manifest narration is that she is compelled to Islam and a new marriage with her husband. The nawadir narration is that she is enslaved in Dar al-Islam and becomes booty for the Muslims, then the husband buys her from the Imam or the Imam gives her to him if he is entitled. Many scholars gave fatwa by this narration and said: 'Whoever examines the conditions of the women of our time and what occurs from them of causes of apostasy repeatedly every day does not hesitate in giving fatwa by the nawadir narration.' However, my father, may Allah have mercy on him, mentioned that it is not possible today to act upon either the manifest narration or the nawadir narration due to the lack of Muslim power to act upon that; there is no way except the opinion given fatwa by the scholars of Samarqand and Bukhara that marriage is not dissolved by her apostasy. (3) Similarly, they gave fatwa by the nawadir narration concerning nidhr al-lijaj (conditional vow), which is a vow suspended upon a matter that the vow-maker wishes to avoid, such as saying: 'If I drink wine, then I must fast for a month.' The manifest narration is that if he drinks wine, he must fulfill the vow only. The nawadir narration is that he is given a choice between fulfilling the vow and expiation, which is the school of al-Shafi'i and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them both. Ibn al-Humam mentioned that it is narrated in al-Nawadir and that it is the choice of the verifiers. And the authors of the texts relied upon that. (4) Similarly, they narrated the manifest narration that the city (misr) is a condition for the enforcement of the judge's ruling, and the nawadir narration that it is not a condition. Then they gave fatwa by the nawadir narration, as Ibn Abidin, may Allah have mercy on him, narrated from al-Bazzaziyyah.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage from 'Usul al-Ifta' discusses a key methodological rule in the Hanafi school: a mufti may prefer a narration that is closer to the hadith evidence, even if it comes from the Nawadir (rare narrations) rather than the Zahir al-Riwayah (the six core books of Imam Muhammad). The text begins by citing the practice of Imam al-Bukhari himself, who selected from Imam Abu Hanifa's rulings what aligned most with hadith. Then Ibn Abidin's principle is presented: rulings from Zahir al-Riwayah are generally followed, but if scholars have explicitly preferred another narration, that is to be followed. The passage then illustrates this with three cases where Hanafi muftis adopted Nawadir rulings. First, the ruling on a wife's apostasy: according to Zahir al-Riwayah she is compelled to Islam and must renew her marriage; the Nawadir enslaves her as war booty, allowing the husband to purchase her back. Many later scholars preferred the Nawadir due to prevalent apostasy, but the author's father noted the impracticality of both positions today, adopting the Samarqandi view that marriage does not dissolve. Second, conditional vows (nidhr al-lajaj): Zahir al-Riwayah requires fulfillment of the vow if the condition occurs; the Nawadir offers a choice between fulfillment and expiation (kaffarah) – a position attributed to Imam Muhammad and al-Shafi'i. Third, the requirement of a defined city (misr) for a judge's ruling: Zahir al-Riwayah makes it necessary; Nawadir says it is not, and this was adopted in fatwa. The passage shows the flexibility within the Hanafi school to respond to changing circumstances while remaining rooted in transmitted evidence.

Key Terms
الروايات النادرة (al-riwayat al-nadirah): Rare or non-mainstream narrations from Imam Muhammad and other Hanafi imams, not part of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The manifest narrations from the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani
نذر اللجاج (nidhr al-lijaj): A vow suspended on a condition that the vow-maker wishes to avoid, intended as a deterrent

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did the author's father reject both the Zahir al-Riwayah and Nawadir positions on wife's apostasy?
A) Because both contradict the Qur'an
B) Because Muslims lack the power to implement them
C) Because women stopped apostatizing
D) Because the Hadith is weak

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufti may shift operative rulings based on practical realities, as seen in the wife's apostasy case where the Samarqandi view became mufta bihi due to Muslim weakness.

Further Applications: Nidhr al-Lijaj and Condition of Misr
Explains the principle of choosing narrations closest to hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Nawadir ruling on nidhr al-lijaj and the requirement of misr for a judge, and explain why later Hanafi scholars preferred these Nawadir positions.

Core Idea
The Nawadir provides flexibility in conditional vows and judicial jurisdiction, and Hanafi muftis have adopted these positions for ease and alignment with hadith.

This lesson presents two additional examples where Hanafi muftis have preferred nawadir narrations: the case of conditional vows (nidhr al-lijaj) and the requirement of a defined city (misr) for a judge's ruling. Both illustrate the school's ability to adopt more practical rulings that are also supported by stronger hadith evidence.

Guided Path
1
Define nidhr al-lijaj
Understand what a conditional vow intended as a deterrent is, and its purpose.
Example: 'If I drink wine, I must fast for a month.'
2
State the two rulings for nidhr
Zahir al-Riwayah: fulfillment required. Nawadir: choice between fulfillment and kaffarah.
The Nawadir aligns with al-Shafi'i and Imam Muhammad's view.
3
Identify the preferred ruling and authority
Who preferred the Nawadir and why? (Ibn al-Humam, authors of matn).
It is 'the choice of the verifiers'.
4
Analyze the misr condition
Zahir al-Riwayah requires misr for a judge's ruling to be enforced; Nawadir says it is not a condition.
Muftis adopted the Nawadir.
5
Identify the common pattern
Both cases show adoption of Nawadir for practicality and alignment with hadith.
The principle from Lesson 1 applies.

Fatwa Based on Nawadir: Practical Examples from Later Hanafi Practice
Lists several cases where fatwa was given based on Nawadir over Zahir al-Riwayah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of shifting fatwa from Zahir al-Riwayah to Nawadir by identifying the circumstances that justify such a shift and giving examples from the text.

Core Idea
Fatwa may shift to Nawadir when Zahir al-Riwayah becomes impractical or opposed to public interest.

This passage presents four specific cases where later Hanafi scholars (mutakhkhirin) issued fatwas based on rare transmissions (Nawadir) rather than the standard authoritative narrations (Zahir al-Riwayah). These examples illustrate that the mufti's duty to balance textual authority with practical needs can lead to adopting weaker transmissions. We will examine each scenario and understand the reasoning behind the shift.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four examples
Read the passage and list the four cases where fatwa was given based on Nawadir: female apostasy, vow of obstinacy, territorial jurisdiction for judge's ruling, and witnessing a woman's acknowledgment.
Look for the key phrase 'وأفتى كثير من المشايخ بهذه الرواية' and similar expressions.
2
Compare Zahir al-Riwayah and Nawadir positions
For each example, note the ruling according to Zahir al-Riwayah and the alternative Nawadir ruling. For instance, in the vow of obstinacy, Zahir al-Riwayah demands fulfillment only, while Nawadir gives a choice between fulfillment and expiation.
Use the text's explicit comparisons.
3
Analyze the reasoning for the shift
Determine why the later scholars chose the Nawadir. The text suggests practical reasons: women's frequent apostasy, the need for flexibility in vows, and the impracticality of requiring territorial jurisdiction or seeing a woman's face.
Consider the maxim 'al-mashaqqah tajlib al-taysir' (hardship brings ease).
4
Note qualifications and exceptions
Observe that in the apostasy case, the author's father noted that neither Zahir nor Nawadir can be acted upon today due to Muslim weakness, so a third position (marriage not dissolved) was adopted. This shows that fatwa can shift even beyond Nawadir.
Not all shifts are permanent; context matters.
5
Extract the general principle
Formulate the rule: The mufti may rely on Nawadir over Zahir al-Riwayah when the latter is impractical or causes hardship, provided the Nawadir does not contradict established principles and is supported by later scholarly consensus.
This is a recognized part of Hanafi fatwa methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
طبقات الفقهاء ورواية النوادر أنها تسترق في دار الإسلام، وتكون فيئاً للمسلمين فيشتريها الزوج من الإمام أو يصرفها إليه لوكان مصرفاً. فأفتى كثير من المشايخ بهذه الرواية وقالوا: "من تصفح أحوال نساء زماننا وما يقع منهن من موجبات الردة مكرراً في كل يوم، لم يتوقف في الإفتاء برواية النوادر (ولكن ذكر والدي رحمه الله تعالى أنه لا يمكن العمل اليوم بظاهر الرواية ولا برواية النوادر، لعدم قوة المسلمين على العمل بذلك، فلا سبيل إلا إلى القول بما أفتى به مشايخ سمرقند وبخارا من أن النكاح لا ينفسخ بردتها. (٣) وكذلك أفتوا برواية النوادر في نذر اللجاج، وهو النذر المعلق على أمر يريد الناذر الاجتناب منه، مثل أن يقول: إن شربت الخمر فعلي صوم شهر. وظاهر الرواية فيه أنه إن شرب الخمر وجب عليه الوفاء لاغير، ورواية النوادر أنه يخير بين الوفاء بالنذر والكفارة، وهو مذهب الشافعي ومحمد رحمهما الله تعالى، وذكر ابن الهمام أنه مروي في النوادر وأنه مختار المحققين ) وعليه مشى أصحاب المتون. (4) وكذلك حكوا ظاهر الرواية أنه يشترط المصر لنفاذ قضاء القاضي. ورواية النوادر أنه ليس بشرط، ثم أفتوا برواية النوادر، كما حكاه ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى عن البزازية. (0) (١) الدر المختار مع حاشية ابن عابدين ٨:٦٤٩ باب نكاح الكافر (٢) جواهر الفقه للعلامة المفتى محمد شفیع رحمه الله تعالى ٢:١٤٦ (٣) فتح القدير ٤:٣٧٥ (٤) رد المختار ١١:٣٢٦ مطلب في أحكام النذر. (ه) رد المحتار ١٦:٥٧٥ باب كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي وكذلك يجب على ظاهر الرواية على من يشهد على إقرار امرأة بشيئ أن كان رأى وجهها عند التحمل. ورواية النوادر أنه لا يشترط رؤية وجهها ) وبه أفتى جمع من العلماء.
Sections of jurists: And the transmission of the Nawadir that she (the apostate) is enslaved in the abode of Islam, and becomes booty for the Muslims, so the husband buys her from the imam or he gives her to him if he is eligible to receive. So many shaykhs gave fatwa according to this transmission and said: 'Whoever examines the conditions of the women of our time and what occurs from them of causes of apostasy repeatedly every day, would not hesitate in giving fatwa according to the Nawadir transmission.' (But my father mentioned that it is not possible to act today by the apparent transmission nor by the Nawadir transmission, due to the lack of strength of the Muslims to act upon that; so there is no way except to adopt the fatwa of the shaykhs of Samarqand and Bukhara that marriage is not dissolved by her apostasy.) (3) Likewise they gave fatwa according to the Nawadir transmission concerning the vow of obstinacy (nadhr al-lijaj), which is a vow suspended on an action that the person wants to avoid, such as saying: 'If I drink wine, then upon me is a month of fasting.' The apparent transmission is that if he drinks wine, he must fulfill (the vow) only. The Nawadir transmission is that he is given a choice between fulfilling the vow and expiation. This is the madhhab of al-Shafi'i and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them). Ibn al-Humam mentioned that it is narrated in the Nawadir and that it is the choice of the verifiers, and upon it the authors of matns proceeded. (4) Likewise they narrated from the apparent transmission that a territorial jurisdiction (misr) is required for the enforcement of a judge's ruling, and the Nawadir transmission is that it is not a condition. Then they gave fatwa according to the Nawadir transmission, as quoted by Ibn Abidin from al-Bazzaziyya. (0) (1) al-Durr al-Mukhtar with Ibn Abidin's Hashiya 8:649, chapter on marriage of disbelievers. (2) Jawahir al-Fiqh by Mufti Muhammad Shafi' 2:146. (3) Fath al-Qadir 4:375. (4) Radd al-Mukhtar 11:326, section on rulings of vows. (5) Radd al-Muhtar 16:575, chapter on the judge's letter to another judge. Likewise it is obligatory according to the apparent transmission for one who testifies to a woman's acknowledgment of something that he had seen her face at the time of bearing witness. The Nawadir transmission is that seeing her face is not a condition, and a group of scholars gave fatwa accordingly.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage from the section on the levels of jurists presents four examples where later Hanafi scholars (the muta'akhkhirin) issued fatwas based on Nawadir (rare or non-mashhur transmissions) rather than the Zahir al-Riwayah (the well-known authoritative transmissions of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani). The first example concerns the apostasy of a woman: according to Zahir al-Riwayah, her marriage is dissolved and she is enslaved; the Nawadir says she is enslaved but the husband can buy her back. Many scholars, observing frequent apostasy in their time, gave fatwa based on the Nawadir. However, the author's father noted that neither position can be acted upon practically due to Muslim weakness, so the fatwa of the Samarqand and Bukhara scholars is adopted: the marriage is not dissolved. The second example is the vow of obstinacy (nathr al-lijaj): Zahir al-Riwayah says only fulfillment is required; Nawadir gives an option between fulfillment and expiation. The third example is the requirement of a territorial jurisdiction (misr) for a judge's ruling to be enforceable: Zahir al-Riwayah requires it; Nawadir does not. The fourth example concerns bearing witness to a woman's acknowledgment: Zahir al-Riwayah requires the witness to have seen her face; Nawadir does not. In all these cases, many later scholars adopted the Nawadir position due to practical needs and changing circumstances. This illustrates the principle that fatwa can shift from the Zahir al-Riwayah to Nawadir when the latter better serves the current context, as long as it does not contradict established principles.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known, authoritative transmissions from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani compiled in the six books of Imam Muhammad.
رواية النوادر (Riwayat al-Nawadir): Rare or less widely transmitted narrations from the early Hanafi imams, often reports by Hasan ibn Ziyad and others, not included in the six core books.
نذر اللجاج (Nadhr al-Lijaj): A vow of obstinacy: a conditional vow made to avoid or prompt a certain action, e.g., 'If I drink wine, I must fast for a month.'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling in the Nawadir transmission regarding a vow of obstinacy (nathr al-lijaj)?
A) The vow must be fulfilled without any alternative.
B) The person is given a choice between fulfilling the vow and paying expiation.
C) The vow is void and nothing is required.
D) Expiation is required without the option of fulfillment.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits fatwa based on Nawadir transmissions when Zahir al-Riwayah proves impractical, as demonstrated by multiple cases from later scholarship.

Using Nawadir When Zahir al-Riwayah Is Silent
Explains the rule for using Nawadir when Zahir al-Riwayah is silent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule for adopting Nawadir rulings when Zahir al-Riwayah is silent, and identify the methodological caution regarding direct attribution from Nawadir manuscripts.

Core Idea
When Zahir al-Riwayah is silent on a ruling, adopt the Nawadir version unless it conflicts with established principles.

This lesson introduces a crucial methodological rule for the Hanafi mufti: what to do when a specific ruling is not found in the six core texts of Zahir al-Riwayah. The answer lies in the secondary source class known as Nawadir, but with important conditions. Through the statements of Ibn Nujaym and Ibn Amir Hajj, you will learn both the default approach and the practical limitations that safeguard the integrity of the school's transmission hierarchy.

Guided Path
1
State the rule
Identify the default approach: when a ruling is not mentioned (maskut anhu) in Zahir al-Riwayah but is present in Nawadir, it is adopted.
This is the general principle stated by Ibn Nujaym.
2
Apply the condition
Recognize the exception: the Nawadir ruling must not contradict the established principles (al-usul al-thabitah) derived from Zahir al-Riwayah.
This condition preserves consistency within the school.
3
Understand the practical limitation
Note Ibn Amir Hajj's caution: direct attribution from Nawadir manuscripts is not permissible; reliance is only on citations in well-known books like al-Hidayah.
This reflects the later school's emphasis on authentic transmission.
4
Work through an example
Apply the rule to the sunnah prayer scenario: one who begins the third rak'ah of the sunnah of Dhuhr and the fard commences should complete the sunnah as four rak'ahs, based on a Nawadir transmission chosen by the shaykhs.
This example is explicitly given in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما إذا كان الحكم مسكوتاً عنه فى ظاهر الرواية، ومذكوراً في النوادر ، فإنّه يؤخذ به، إلا أن يكون خلافاً للأصول الثابتة فى ظاهر الرواية. قال ابن نجيم رحمه الله تعالى: "المسألة حيث لم تذكر فى ظاهر الرواية وثبتت في رواية أخرى تعين المصير إليها. ( ومنه ما روى فى النوادر أن الذي شرع في الركعة الثالثة من سنة الظهر أو الجمعة، وقيدها بالسجدة، وقامت الصلوة، فإنه يتمها أربعاً. وهو الذي اختاره المشايخ (۳) والمسائل من هذا القبيل كثيرة تجدها في المحيط البرهاني كما سيأتى إن شاء الله تعالى. وقال ابن أمير حاج رحمه الله تعالى: "لووجد بعض نسخ النوادر فى زماننا، لا يحل عزوما فيها إلى محمد ولا إلى أبي يوسف، لأنها لم تشتهر في عصرنا في ديارنا ولم تتداول. نعم ! إذا وجد النقل عن النوادر مثلاً في كتاب مشهورٍ معروف كالهداية والمبسوط، كان ذلك تعويلاً على ذلك الكتاب.
As for the case where the ruling is not mentioned in the Zahir al-Riwayah, but is mentioned in the Nawadir, then it is taken, unless it contradicts the established principles in the Zahir al-Riwayah. Ibn Nujaym (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'When a matter is not mentioned in the Zahir al-Riwayah but is established in another transmission, it is necessary to resort to it.' Among that is what is narrated in the Nawadir that a person who has begun the third rak'ah of the sunnah of Dhuhr or Jumu'ah, and has bound it by prostration, and the obligatory prayer has commenced, then he completes it as four (rak'ahs). This is what the shaykhs chose. (3) And matters of this kind are many; you find them in al-Muhit al-Burhani, as will come later, God willing. And Ibn Amir Hajj (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'If some copies of the Nawadir were found in our time, it would not be permissible to attribute from them to Muhammad or to Abu Yusuf, because they are not well-known in our time in our lands and have not been circulated. Yes! If the transmission from the Nawadir is found, for example, in a well-known and famous book like al-Hidayah and al-Mabsut, then the reliance is on that book.'
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage establishes a key methodological rule for the Hanafi fatwa process: when a particular ruling is not addressed in the Zahir al-Riwayah (the core authoritative texts of the school), but is found in the Nawadir (rare transmissions), the ruling from the Nawadir is to be adopted, provided it does not contradict the established principles (usul) of the Zahir al-Riwayah. Ibn Nujaym affirms this principle, stating that one must resort to the other transmission. The author provides a concrete example: if someone begins the third rak'ah of the four-rak'ah sunnah of Dhuhr or Jumu'ah (i.e., the sunnah mu'akkada before the fard), and has performed the sajdah of that rak'ah, then the congregation starts the fard prayer, the person should complete the sunnah as four rak'ahs (i.e., finish it as a full prayer, not cut short), according to a Nawadir transmission. The shaykhs chose this ruling. The passage also includes an important caution from Ibn Amir Hajj: if someone in later times finds an original manuscript of the Nawadir, it is not permissible to directly attribute rulings from it to Imam Muhammad or Abu Yusuf, because those texts are not widely known and authenticated in the later period. However, if the Nawadir ruling is cited in a famous and reliable book like al-Hidayah or al-Mabsut, one may rely on that citation, because the later authority of the book certifies the transmission. This shows the layered authority in the Hanafi school: the immediate source of fatwa is not the original Nawadir text but its inclusion in the post-classical authoritative works.

Key Terms
مسكوت عنه (maskut 'anhu): A ruling that is not mentioned or discussed in the given source, here specifically in the Zahir al-Riwayah texts.
الأصول الثابتة (al-usul al-thabitah): The established principles or foundational rules derived from the Zahir al-Riwayah, which must not be violated by a Nawadir ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Amir Hajj, what is the condition for directly attributing a ruling to Muhammad al-Shaybani from the Nawadir?
A) The Nawadir manuscript must be in the original handwriting of Imam Muhammad.
B) The Nawadir transmission must be cited in a well-known book like al-Hidayah or al-Mabsut.
C) The ruling must be confirmed by a consensus of the Companions.
D) The ruling must be found in the Zahir al-Riwayah as well.

Key Takeaway
When Zahir al-Riwayah is silent, adopt the Nawadir ruling unless it contradicts established usul; and only rely on Nawadir if it is cited in authoritative post-classical works.

Witnessing a Woman's Face: Zahir al-Riwayah vs Nawadir
Intra-Hanafi difference on witness identification requirement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the ruling on witnessing a woman's face in Zahir al-Riwayah and Nawadir, and apply the principle that a Nawadir ruling may be used for fatwa when supported by a group of scholars.

Core Idea
A mufti may follow a Nawadir ruling even if Zahir al-Riwayah differs, when endorsed by reputable scholars.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hanafi tradition: whether a witness to a woman's acknowledgment must have seen her face at the time of hearing it. The passage contrasts the position of Zahir al-Riwayah (the core transmitted corpus) with that of Nawadir (rare transmissions), and notes that a group of later scholars issued fatwas based on the Nawadir view. This illustrates the principle that Nawadir can have operative authority in fatwa, even when it departs from the standard transmission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling in each transmission
Read the passage and note that the act is bearing witness to a woman's acknowledgment. In Zahir al-Riwayah, the witness must have seen her face at the time of hearing (tahammul). In Nawadir, it is not required.
The key phrase is 'عند التحمل' (at the time of bearing witness).
2
Distinguish authority between Zahir al-Riwayah and Nawadir
Zahir al-Riwayah is the highest authoritative corpus; Nawadir is lower but can be acted upon. The passage shows that a group of scholars gave fatwa by Nawadir, indicating it is permissible to follow in practice.
This is an example of tarjih (preference) within the school.
3
Apply the fatwa hierarchy principle
A mufti must know which transmission is operative. Here, despite Zahir al-Riwayah's stricter requirement, the Nawadir position is relied upon by those scholars. This teaches that Nawadir can be used when supported by scholarly consensus or need.
The principle is: Fatwa may follow Nawadir if it is not contradicted by stronger evidence and has scholarly backing.

Source Text

وكذلك يجب على ظاهر الرواية على من يشهد على إقرار امرأة بشيء أن كان رأى وجهها عند التحمل. ورواية النوادر أنه لا يشترط رؤية وجهها، وبه أفتى جمع من العلماء.
Similarly, it is required according to Zahir al-Riwayah for one who bears witness to a woman's acknowledgment of something that he had seen her face at the time of bearing witness. And the narration of Nawadir is that seeing her face is not a condition, and a group of scholars gave fatwa by it.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage presents a specific ruling illustrating the difference between Zahir al-Riwayah and Nawadir. In Zahir al-Riwayah (the core transmitted corpus), a witness to a woman's acknowledgment must have seen her face at the time of hearing the acknowledgment, ensuring proper identification. However, in the Nawadir (rare transmissions), this condition is not required. A group of later Hanafi scholars issued fatwas according to the Nawadir position, showing that Nawadir can be relied upon for fatwa, though it is not part of the authoritative corpus. This exemplifies the methodological principle that fatwa may follow Nawadir if Zahir al-Riwayah is silent or its ruling is not absolutely settled.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The established transmitted corpus of the Hanafi school, primarily the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
النوادر (al-Nawadir): Rare transmissions that are not part of Zahir al-Riwayah, often from Hasan ibn Ziyad and others.

In the Hanafi school, a mufti may follow a Nawadir ruling even if it differs from Zahir al-Riwayah, when it is supported by a group of scholars.

Acting on Nawadir When Zahir al-Riwayah is Silent
Methodological rule for adopting Nawadir rulings when Zahir al-Riwayah has no ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that Nawadir rulings are acted upon when Zahir al-Riwayah is silent, and identify the exception when the Nawadir contradicts established principles.

Core Idea
When Zahir al-Riwayah is silent, refer to Nawadir — unless it contradicts established principles.

In Hanafi fatwa methodology, the mufti must know which sources to rely upon when the core corpus (Zahir al-Riwayah) does not address a case. This lesson introduces a key rule: the Nawadir (rare transmissions) fill the gap, but only as long as they do not undermine the foundational principles of the madhhab. Understanding this rule equips you to navigate cases where the standard texts are silent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue in Zahir al-Riwayah
Check the six core books of Imam Muhammad (al-Asl, al-Jami' al-Saghir, etc.) for the ruling. If the matter is mentioned, that ruling is binding. If silent, proceed.
Silence here means no explicit ruling, not a contradictory ruling.
2
Locate the ruling in Nawadir
Search the Nawadir collections (e.g., reports of Hasan ibn Ziyad, etc.). If a ruling is found, it is prima facie adoptable.
Nawadir literally means 'rare' but here it refers to transmissions outside Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Check for contradiction with usul
Evaluate whether the Nawadir ruling conflicts with the established principles (usul) of Zahir al-Riwayah. If it does, reject it; if not, adopt it.
The usul include general maxims, not just specific rulings.
4
Apply the rule to a concrete case
Use the example from the text: a person starts the third rak'ah of sunnah Zuhr/Jumu'ah and then fard is established. According to Nawadir, he completes four rak'ahs. This does not contradict any principle of Zahir al-Riwayah, so it is adopted.
The mashayikh (later scholars) chose this view, confirming its operative status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما إذا كان الحكم مسكوتاً عنه في ظاهر الرواية، ومذكوراً في النوادر، فإنه يؤخذ به، إلا أن يكون خلافاً للأصول الثابتة في ظاهر الرواية. قال ابن نجيم رحمه الله تعالى: "المسألة حيث لم تذكر في ظاهر الرواية وثبتت في رواية أخرى تعين المصير إليها." ومنه ما روى في النوادر أن الذي شرع في الركعة الثالثة من سنة الظهر أو الجمعة، وقيدها بالسجدة، وقامت الصلاة، فإنه يتمها أربعاً. وهو الذي اختاره المشايخ. والمسائل من هذا القبيل كثيرة تجدها في المحيط البرهاني كما سيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى.
As for when the ruling is not mentioned in Zahir al-Riwayah and is mentioned in Nawadir, then it is acted upon, unless it contradicts the established principles of Zahir al-Riwayah. Ibn Nujaym (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'When a matter is not mentioned in Zahir al-Riwayah and is established in another narration, it is necessary to refer to it.' From this is what was narrated in Nawadir: that one who begins the third rak'ah of the sunnah of Zuhr or Jumu'ah, and ties it with the prostration, and the prayer is established (i.e., the congregational prayer begins), then he completes it as four (rak'ahs). And this is what the mashayikh chose. And there are many cases like this; you will find them in al-Muhit al-Burhani, as will come, Allah willing.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage establishes a key methodological rule for Hanafi fatwa: when a legal ruling is absent from Zahir al-Riwayah (the core authoritative corpus) but is found in Nawadir (rare transmissions), the mufti adopts the Nawadir ruling. However, this is subject to an important condition: the Nawadir ruling must not contradict the foundational principles (usul) that are firmly established in Zahir al-Riwayah. Ibn Nujaym explicitly states that in such cases, it is obligatory (ta'ayyana) to refer to the Nawadir. The passage provides a concrete application: a person who has started the third rak'ah of the sunnah prayer of Zuhr or Jumu'ah, and then the congregational prayer (fard) is commenced, should complete his sunnah as four rak'ahs (i.e., as if he intended to pray four from the start) according to Nawadir, and this was chosen by the later mashayikh (senior scholars). This shows that Nawadir can fill gaps in the madhhab's transmitted rulings.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The core transmitted corpus of the Hanafi school (six books of Imam Muhammad).
النوادر (al-Nawadir): Rare transmissions outside Zahir al-Riwayah, often from Hasan ibn Ziyad and others.
المشايخ (al-Mashayikh): Later authoritative scholars of the Hanafi school who weighed and chose rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) He must prefer the opinion of Abu Hanifa.
D) He must make ijtihad from scratch.

Key Takeaway
The mufti must adopt Nawadir rulings when Zahir al-Riwayah is silent, provided they do not contradict the established principles of the school.

Caution in Attributing Nawadir Rulings
Warning against attributing Nawadir rulings directly to early imams if manuscripts are unknown

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a ruling from Nawadir is acceptable for fatwa according to the Hanafi rasm al-mufti and apply Ibn Amir Hajj's distinction between direct attribution and reliance on well-known books.

Core Idea
A Nawadir ruling cannot be attributed to early imams unless transmitted through a widely known authoritative book.

Muftis must be scrupulous about the sources they cite. Ibn Amir Hajj provides a critical caution regarding Nawadir texts—rare transmissions outside Zahir al-Riwayah. In this lesson, you will learn the boundaries of acceptable attribution and the role of well-known secondary sources like al-Hidayah in verifying Nawadir rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibition
State what Ibn Amir Hajj forbids: directly attributing rulings from an obscure Nawadir manuscript to Imam Muhammad or Abu Yusuf.
The prohibition applies when the manuscript is not widely known or circulated.
2
Understand the reasoning
Explain why it is prohibited: the transmission of Nawadir is not verified, and the text has not been widely accepted in the madhhab.
Attribution requires a known chain (sanad) or widespread acceptance (shuhrah).
3
Locate the exception
Identify when it becomes permissible: when the same ruling is quoted in a famous, authoritative book like al-Hidayah or al-Mabsut.
The reliance is then on the famous book, not the original Nawadir manuscript.
4
Determine the basis of reliance
Clarify the legal basis: the ruling is attributed to the intermediate book (ta'wil 'ala dhalika al-kitab), not directly to the early imams.
This preserves the chain of authority and ensures reliability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال ابن أمير حاج رحمه الله تعالى: "لو وجد بعض نسخ النوادر في زماننا، لا يحل عزو ما فيها إلى محمد ولا إلى أبي يوسف، لأنها لم تشتهر في عصرنا في ديارنا ولم تتداول. نعم! إذا وجد النقل عن النوادر مثلاً في كتاب مشهور معروف كالهداية والمبسوط، كان ذلك تعويلاً على ذلك الكتاب."
And Ibn Amir Hajj (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'If some copies of Nawadir are found in our time, it is not permissible to attribute what is in them to Muhammad or to Abu Yusuf, because they have not become famous in our era in our lands and were not circulated. Yes! If a transmission from Nawadir is found, for example, in a well-known famous book like al-Hidayah and al-Mabsut, then that is reliance on that book.'
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage provides an important practical restriction on using Nawadir literature for fatwa. Ibn Amir Hajj warns that if an obscure manuscript of Nawadir is discovered in later times, one cannot simply attribute rulings from it directly to Imam Muhammad or Abu Yusuf because the transmission was never widely known or verified. This caution preserves the integrity of the madhhab by preventing unverified attributions. However, he provides an exception: if the Nawadir content is cited in a well-known and recognized book like al-Hidayah or al-Mabsut, then the attribution is valid because it is based on the authority of that trusted compilation. This principle ensures that fatwa is based on reliable, widespread sources.

Key Terms
النوادر (al-Nawadir): Rare transmission texts distinct from Zahir al-Riwayah.
تعويل (ta'wil): Reliance (here: reliance on the well-known book, not directly on Nawadir).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Amir Hajj, when is it permissible to rely on a ruling from Nawadir?
A) When any manuscript of Nawadir is found, no matter the source.
B) When the ruling is also supported by qiyas.
C) When the Nawadir content is found in a famous book like al-Hidayah or al-Mabsut.
D) When the ruling is from the companions of Abu Hanifa.

Key Takeaway
A Nawadir ruling is only acceptable for fatwa when it is transmitted through a well-known authoritative book, not directly from an obscure manuscript.

The Four Categories of Hanafi Legal Materials
Classification of Hanafi rulings by authority for fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four layers of Hanafi rulings according to Shah Wali Allah's classification and apply their hierarchy when determining the authoritative position for fatwa.

Core Idea
The authority of a Hanafi ruling depends on its source layer: Zahir al-Riwaya unconditionally accepted, rare transmissions only if aligned with principles, later deductions by consensus always, and disputed later deductions conditionally.

In this passage, Shah Wali Allah al-Dihlawi provides a crucial classification of Hanafi legal materials into four categories based on their source and authority. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for a mufti to correctly weigh conflicting rulings. The passage also clarifies a historical point about two major Hanafi compilations, Al-Muhit al-Burhani and Al-Muhit al-Radawi, setting the stage for the classification.

Guided Path
1
Understand the historical context
Note that the author clarifies a mistake: Al-Muhit al-Burhani is the organized work with Zahir al-Riwaya first, not Al-Muhit al-Radawi. This background is important for later scholars' citations.
2
Identify the first category: Zahir al-Riwaya
This comprises rulings in the six core works of Imam Muhammad. They are accepted unconditionally, even if they appear to contradict general principles of the madhhab.
The Hidayah author may exert effort to reconcile such cases.
3
Identify the second category: Rare transmissions (riwaya shadhdha)
These are anomalous reports from the early imams. They are accepted only if they agree with established principles. Al-Hidayah sometimes corrects them when evidence supports.
4
Identify the third and fourth categories: Takhrij of later scholars
Third: deductions agreed upon by the majority of later scholars (jumhur) — accepted unconditionally. Fourth: deductions lacking consensus — mufti must test them against principles and parallels (nazair) from earlier authorities; accept only if conforming.
The fourth category requires careful evaluation by the mufti.

قال العبد الضعيف عفا الله عنه: هذا ما ذكره ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى بالنسبة لمحيط رضئ الدين السَّرَحْسِى والظاهر أنه لم يطلع عليه بنفسه، ولا على المحيط البرهاني. والحقيقة التي ظهرت بعد طباعة المحيط البرهاني: أن هذا الوصف يصدق عليه دون محيط رضى الدين السِّرَحْسِى. فإنّه قال الإمام برهان الدين فى مقدمة محيطه: "وجمعت مسائل المبسوط والجامعين والسير والزيادات، وألحقت فيها مسائل النوادر والفتاوى ،والواقعات وضممت إليها من الفوائد التي استفدتها من سيدى مولاى والدى تغمّده الله تعالى بالرحمة والدقائق التي حفظتها من مشايخ زمانی وفصلت الكتاب تفصيلاً، وجنست المسائل تجنيساً. (۲) وذكر محقق الكتاب ابن أختى الشيخ نعيم أشرف حفظه الله تعالى أنه اطلع على نُسخةٍ من المحيط الرضوى، وقال: "طالعت بعض المواضع منها، فوجدت المسائل فيها ممزوجةً غير مرتبة خلاف ما سمعت ورأيت في كلام بعض المشايخ أنهم ذكروا أن رضى الدين السرخسي ميّز ورتب المسائل، فذكر أوّلاً مسائل ظاهر الرواية، ثم النوادر والفتاوى والواقعات بل وجدت هذه الميزة تماماً فى المحيط البرهاني وقد طبع الكتاب والحمد لله تعالى بتحقيقه، فوجد الأمر كما وصف.
قسیم
الشيخ ولى الله الدهلوى لمسائل الحنفية وقد قسم الشيخ ولي الله المحدّث الدهلوي رحمه الله تعالى طبقاتِ المسائل على أربعة أقسام: الأول: قسم تقرر في ظاهر الرواية. وحكمه أنهم يقبلونه في كل حال، وافقت الأصول أو خالفت قال: " ولذلك ترى صاحب الهداية وغيره يتكلفون بيان الفرق في مسائل التجنيس "
والقسم الثانى هو رواية شاذة عن أبى حنيفة وصاحبيه وحكمه أن لا يقبلوه إلا إذا وافق الأصول. قال: " وكم فى الهداية ونحوها من تصحيح لبعض الروايات الشاذة لحال الدليل."
والقسمُ الثَّالث هو تخريج المتأخرين، اتفق عليه جمهور الأصحاب، وحكمه أنّهم يُفتون به على كل حال.
والقسم الرابع: هو تخريج المتأخرين، لم يتفق عليه جمهور الأصحاب، وحكمه أنّ المفتي يعرضه على الأصول و النظائر من كلام السلف، فإن وجده موافقاً للأصول والنظائر أخذ به وإلا تركه (۳)
ونقل الإمام عبد الحي اللكنوي رحمه الله تعالى تقسيم الشيخ ولي الله الدهلوي هذا ثم قال: "لعلك تتفطن من هذا البحث أنه ليس كل ما في (عقد الجيد في أحكام الاجتهاد والتقليد ص ٤١)
The weak slave, may Allah pardon him, said: This is what Ibn Abidin, may Allah have mercy on him, mentioned regarding the Muhit of Radhi al-Din al-Sarakhsi, and apparently he did not see it himself, nor the Muhit al-Burhani. The truth that became apparent after the printing of Muhit al-Burhani is that this description applies to it, not to the Muhit of Radhi al-Din al-Sarakhsi. Indeed, Imam Burhan al-Din said in the introduction to his Muhit: "I collected the issues of al-Mabsut, al-Jami'ayn, al-Siyar, and al-Ziyadat, and appended to them the issues of al-Nawadir, al-Fatawa, and al-Waqi'at, and added to them benefits I obtained from my master my father (may Allah envelop him in mercy) and the subtleties I preserved from my teachers of my time, and I detailed the book in detail, and classified the issues by classification." (2) And the editor of the book, my nephew Shaykh Nu'aym Ashraf (may Allah preserve him), mentioned that he saw a copy of al-Muhit al-Radawi and said: "I examined some parts of it, and found the issues there intermixed and unordered, contrary to what I heard and saw in the speech of some shaykhs that they mentioned that Radhi al-Din al-Sarakhsi distinguished and ordered the issues, so he first mentioned the issues of Zahir al-Riwaya, then al-Nawadir, al-Fatawa, and al-Waqi'at. Rather, I found this distinction entirely in al-Muhit al-Burhani, and the book has been printed, praise be to Allah, by his editing, and I found the matter as described."

Section:
Shah Wali Allah al-Dihlawi on Hanafi issues: And Shaykh Wali Allah al-Muhaddith al-Dihlawi, may Allah have mercy on him, divided the layers of issues into four sections: 
First: The section established in Zahir al-Riwaya. Its ruling is that they accept it in every case, whether it agrees with principles or opposes them. He said: "Therefore you see the author of al-Hidayah and others exerting themselves to explain the difference in issues of classification."
Second: The section is a rare transmission (riwaya shadhdha) from Abu Hanifa and his two companions. Its ruling is that they do not accept it unless it agrees with principles. He said: "How many instances are there in al-Hidayah and similar works of correcting some rare transmissions due to evidence."
Third: The section is the deduction (takhrij) of the later scholars, agreed upon by the majority of the companions. Its ruling is that they give fatwa by it in every case.
Fourth: The section is the deduction of the later scholars, not agreed upon by the majority of the companions. Its ruling is that the mufti presents it to the principles and parallels from the speech of the predecessors; if he finds it agreeing with the principles and parallels, he adopts it; otherwise he leaves it. (3)
And Imam Abd al-Hayy al-Laknawi, may Allah have mercy on him, transmitted this division of Shaykh Wali Allah al-Dihlawi and then said: "Perhaps you will realize from this discussion that not everything in..." (from 'Iqd al-Jayyid fi Ahkam al-Ijtihad wa al-Taqlid, p. 41)
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Ifta discusses the classification of Hanafi legal materials according to their authority, primarily drawing from Shah Wali Allah al-Dihlawi's division. The author first clarifies a factual point about two major Hanafi compilations: Al-Muhit al-Burhani and Al-Muhit al-Radawi. Ibn Abidin had described Al-Muhit al-Radawi as organized with first issues of Zahir al-Riwaya, then Nawadir, but after examining the printed Al-Muhit al-Burhani, the author finds that organization actually belongs to Al-Muhit al-Burhani, while Al-Muhit al-Radawi is intermixed. This sets the stage for the main topic: the hierarchical categorization of Hanafi fiqh for fatwa purposes. Shah Wali Allah divides all Hanafi legal rulings into four categories. First are those established in Zahir al-Riwaya (the six core works of Imam Muhammad), which are accepted unconditionally regardless of whether they align with general principles (usul), because they are the primary transmitted texts. Second are rare or anomalous transmissions (riwaya shadhdha) from the early imams; these are only accepted if they align with established principles, and the author of al-Hidayah sometimes corrects them when evidence supports them. Third are deductions (takhrij) by later scholars that have gained consensus of the majority (jumhur) of the madhhab; these are accepted unconditionally. Fourth are deductions by later scholars that lack such consensus; these require the mufti to test them against the principles and precedents (nazair) from earlier authorities, accepting them only if they conform. This classification is crucial for a mufti to determine the binding weight of any given ruling.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwaya): The transmitted rulings found in the six core works of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, and al-Ziyadat.
رواية شاذة (riwaya shadhdha): A rare or anomalous transmission from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, or Muhammad al-Shaybani that is not part of the established corpus.
تخريج المتأخرين (takhrij al-muta'akhkhirin): Rulings derived by later Hanafi scholars (from the 6th century AH onward) through deduction from the principles of the madhhab, not directly transmitted from the early imams.
طبقات المسائل (tabaqat al-masa'il): The hierarchical layers of Hanafi rulings based on their source and authority in the madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Shah Wali Allah's classification, what is the ruling on a Hanafi legal issue that belongs to the third category (takhrij al-muta'akhkhirin agreed upon by the majority)?
A) It is accepted only if it agrees with principles.
B) It is accepted unconditionally in every case.
C) It must be presented to the principles and parallels before being accepted.
D) It is never accepted because it is from later scholars.

Key Takeaway
The mufti must classify any Hanafi ruling into one of four authority layers: Zahir al-Riwaya (unconditional), rare transmissions (conditional), agreed-upon later deductions (unconditional), or disputed later deductions (conditional).

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Shah Waliullah's Four Categories of Hanafi Rulings
Classification of Hanafi rulings into four tiers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify each of Shah Waliullah's four categories of Hanafi rulings and apply the appropriate fatwa rule for each category.

Core Idea
Not everything in a fatwa collection is the madhhab — only Zahir al-Riwayah is binding unconditionally.

Shah Waliullah Dehlawi's four-tier hierarchy is the master key to navigating Hanafi fatwa literature. Understanding it prevents the mufti from attributing later derived opinions directly to Imam Abu Hanifa. This passage establishes a methodological rule (rasm al-mufti) that guides the mufti in weighing the authority of different legal transmissions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories and their definitions
Read the passage and list the four categories: (1) Zahir al-Riwayah, (2) Rare transmission, (3) Takhrīj with consensus of the majority, (4) Takhrīj without consensus. Note the key characteristic of each.
Focus on the ruling (hukm) for each category.
2
Understand the mufti's obligation for each category
For each category, determine what action the mufti must take: unconditional acceptance (category 1), conditional acceptance (category 2), unconditional acceptance (category 3), or evaluation against principles and precedents (category 4).
Categories 1 and 3 are binding even if they contradict general principles.
3
Analyze the water basin example
Examine al-Laknawi's example: the ruling about 'the tenth in the tenth' basin. Note that later fatwa collections adopted a different ruling, but the original madhhab is something else. This illustrates the danger of conflating takhrīj with the direct madhhab.
The example shows that even widely accepted rulings may not be from Abu Hanifa himself.
4
Apply the classification to a hypothetical scenario
Given a ruling found in a later fatwa collection, determine which category it likely belongs to based on its source and whether it was subject to broad acceptance or not.
Use the principles from al-Laknawi's warning to avoid misattribution.

قسیم
الشيخ ولى الله الدهلوى لمسائل الحنفية وقد قسم الشيخ ولي الله المحدّث الدهلوي رحمه الله تعالى طبقاتِ المسائل على أربعة أقسام: الأول: قسم تقرر في ظاهر الرواية. وحكمه أنهم يقبلونه في كل حال، وافقت الأصول أو خالفت قال: " ولذلك ترى صاحب الهداية وغيره يتكلفون بيان الفرق في مسائل التجنيس "
والقسم الثانى هو رواية شاذة عن أبى حنيفة وصاحبيه وحكمه أن لا يقبلوه إلا إذا وافق الأصول. قال: " وكم فى الهداية ونحوها من تصحيح لبعض الروايات الشاذة لحال الدليل."
والقسمُ الثَّالث هو تخريج المتأخرين، اتفق عليه جمهور الأصحاب، وحكمه أنّهم يُفتون به على كل حال.
والقسم الرابع: هو تخريج المتأخرين، لم يتفق عليه جمهور الأصحاب، وحكمه أنّ المفتي يعرضه على الأصول و النظائر من كلام السلف، فإن وجده موافقاً للأصول والنظائر أخذ به وإلا تركه.
ونقل الإمام عبد الحي اللكنوي رحمه الله تعالى تقسيم الشيخ ولي الله الدهلوي هذا ثم قال: "لعلك تتفطن من هذا البحث أنه ليس كل ما في الفتاوى المعتبرة المختلفة، كالخلاصة والظهيريّة وفتاوى قاضي خان وغيرها من الفتاوى التى لم يميّز أصحابها بين المذهب والتخريج وغيره، قول أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه، بل منها ما هو منقول عنهم، ومنها ما هو مستنبط الفقها ومنها ما هو مخرج الفقهاء، فيجب على الناظر فيها أن لا يتجاسر على نسبة كل ما فيها إليهم، بل يميز بين ما هو قولهم وبين ما هو مخرج بعدهم. ومن لم يميز بين ذلك وبين هذا أشكل الأمر عليه ألا ترى فى مسئلة العشر في العشر في بحث الحياض، فإن الفتاوى مملوؤة باعتباره، والفتوى عليه، مع أنه ليس مذهب صاحب المذهب، وإنّما مذهبه كما صرح به محمد محمد في الموطأ وقدماء أصحابنا هو أنه لو كان الحوض بحيث لا يتحرك أحد جوانبه بتحريك الجانب الآخر لا يتنجس بوقوع النّجاسة فيه وإلا يتنجس. ومن لم يتفطنه وظنّ أنّه مذهب صاحب المذهب، تعسر عليه تأصيله على أصل شرعي معتمد عليه.
ثم ذكر الإمام اللكنوى تقسيماً آخر لمسائل الحنفية بحسب قوة الدليل، وذكر أنه إذا تبين للعالم فى مسألةٍ أن مذهب إمامه يُعارض جديثاً صحيحاً فإنّه يعمل بما وافق الحديث، وبهذا لا يخرحُ عن التقليد. وهذا إنّما يتأتى فيمن يصلح للنظر فى الدلائل وقدمنا شروطها وآدابها في مبحث التقليد. وأمّا المُفتى الحنفي المقلّد الذى لا يستطيع النظر في ذلك يجب عليه أن يلتزم بقواعد رسم المفتى التى شرحها العلامة ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى في شرح عقود رسم المفتى. ونُريد الآن أن نأتي بتلك القواعد بتلخيص وبشيئ من الشرح والإيضاح من مصادر أخرى. والله سبحانه هو الموفق.
Division: Shaykh Wali Allah al-Dihlawi divided Hanafi issues into four categories: First: what is established in Zahir al-Riwayah. Its ruling: they accept it in every case, whether it agrees with principles or opposes them. He said: 'Thus you see the author of al-Hidayah and others taking pains to explain the difference in matters of tajnis.' Second category: a rare transmission (riwaya shādhdha) from Abu Hanifa and his companions. Its ruling: they do not accept it unless it agrees with principles. He said: 'How often in al-Hidayah and similar works is there correction of some rare transmissions due to the strength of evidence.' Third category: takhrīj of the later scholars that the majority of companions agreed upon. Its ruling: they give fatwa by it in any case. Fourth category: takhrīj of the later scholars that the majority of companions did not agree upon. Its ruling: the mufti presents it to the principles and parallels from the statements of the predecessors; if he finds it agreeing with principles and parallels, he adopts it, otherwise he leaves it. Imam Abdul Hayy al-Laknawi (may Allah have mercy on him) transmitted this division and said: 'You may realize from this research that not everything in the various reliable fatwa collections, such as al-Khulāsa, al-Ẓahīriyya, Fatāwā Qāḍī Khān, and other fatwa books whose authors did not distinguish between the madhhab and takhrīj and others, is the saying of Abu Hanifa and his two companions. Rather, some are transmitted from them, some are deduced by jurists, and some are derived by jurists. Thus it is incumbent upon the one who looks into them not to dare to attribute everything in them to them, but to distinguish between what is their saying and what is derived after them. Whoever does not distinguish between this and that, the matter will become difficult for him. Do you not see the issue of 'the tenth in the tenth' in the discussion of basins? The fatwa collections are filled with considering it and giving fatwa accordingly, even though it is not the madhhab of the imam of the madhhab. Rather, his madhhab—as Muhammad expressly stated in al-Muwatta and the early companions—is that if the basin is such that one side does not move when the other side is moved, it does not become impure by the falling of impurity into it; otherwise it becomes impure. Whoever does not realize this and thinks it is the madhhab of the imam, it will be difficult for him to base it on a reliable shar'i principle.' Then Imam al-Laknawi mentioned another division of Hanafi issues according to the strength of evidence, stating that if a scholar becomes clear in an issue that the madhhab of his imam contradicts an authentic hadith, he should act in accordance with the hadith, and by this he does not depart from taqlid. This applies to one who is competent to consider evidences, whose conditions and etiquettes we have already mentioned in the section on taqlid. As for the Hanafi muqallid mufti who is unable to consider that, he must adhere to the rules of Rasm al-Mufti that Allama Ibn Abidin explained in Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. Now we intend to present those rules in summary with some explanation and clarification from other sources. Allah Almighty is the Granter of success.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage is a classification of Hanafi legal rulings into four categories according to Shah Waliullah Dehlawi (d. 1176 AH), a seminal figure in Islamic scholarship. It is a methodological rule (rasm al-mufti) that helps muftis navigate the Hanafi tradition. The first category is Zahir al-Riwayah—the most authoritative layer, established in the six books of Imam Muhammad. These rulings are binding even if they appear inconsistent with general principles; scholars like the author of al-Hidayah exert effort to explain apparent contradictions (e.g., in the issue of tajnis—where the same case appears in multiple chapters). The second category is a rare transmission (riwaya shādhdha) from Abu Hanifa or his companions that does not match the well-known narration. Such transmissions are only accepted if they align with established principles (usul). The third category is takhrīj (derivation) by later scholars that gained consensus agreement among the majority of Hanafi jurists. These are accepted unconditionally. The fourth category is takhrīj that lacks consensus; the mufti must evaluate it against principles and precedents from early authorities. Imam Abdul Hayy al-Laknawi (d. 1304 AH) underscores the danger of assuming all sayings in fatwa collections represent Imam Abu Hanifa's own view. He gives the example of the rule regarding a basin of water less than ten cubits by ten cubits: the prevalent fatwa in later books says it remains pure if impurity falls unless one side moves? Actually, the example is about 'the tenth in the tenth'—a basin of ten by ten cubits. The early Hanafi position is that if the basin is so large that moving one side does not move the other, it does not become impure; otherwise it does. But later fatwa books often ruled differently, based on takhrīj. A mufti must be aware of this. Finally, al-Laknawi mentions that a qualified scholar may set aside the madhhab if it contradicts a sahih hadith, but this is only for those capable of independent analysis (i.e., a mujtahid within the madhhab). The ordinary mufti must follow the rules of Rasm al-Mufti as codified by Ibn Abidin, which the author will now summarize.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The most authoritative layer of Hanafi rulings, transmitted in the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
رواية شاذة (riwaya shādhdha): A rare transmission from Abu Hanifa or his two companions that contradicts the well-known narrations.
تخريج المتأخرين (takhrij al-muta'akhkhirin): Derived rulings from later Hanafi jurists based on principles or analogy, not directly transmitted from the founders.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Shah Waliullah's classification, what is the ruling of a mufti regarding a ruling from the first category (Zahir al-Riwayah)?
A) He must adopt it only if it agrees with principles.
B) He must adopt it unconditionally, even if it contradicts principles.
C) He must evaluate it against principles and parallels.
D) He must reject it because it is rare.

Key Takeaway
Zahir al-Riwayah is the foundational layer of Hanafi law and must be applied unconditionally, while later derivations require careful scrutiny.

Distinguishing the Madhhab from Later Derivations: A Mufti's Warning
Warning to muftis about mixing madhhab layers with example of water basin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the difference between the original Hanafi madhhab and later juristic derivations, and apply the criterion of authenticity to avoid issuing fatwas contrary to the school's foundation.

Core Idea
A fatwa collection is not the madhhab — the mufti must trace each ruling back to the founding imams.

This passage opens with a critical instruction for any Hanafi mufti: not all rulings in popular fatwa collections represent the authentic madhhab of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. Many are later ijtihad (takhrij) by subsequent jurists. The author illustrates this with a concrete example from the chapter on impurities in water basins, showing how a widely adopted rule ('a tenth of a tenth') contradicts the actual position of Imam Muhammad. The lesson equips you with the mindset to distinguish layers within the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
Recognize that fatwa collections like al-Khulasa and Fatawa Qadi Khan mix original madhhab rulings with later deductions. The mufti must not assume every ruling there is from the imams.
The passage explicitly warns: 'لا يتجاسر على نسبة كل ما فيها إليهم'.
2
Understand the imperative
The mufti must distinguish between what is the actual statement of the imams and what is a later derivation (takhrij).
The author emphasizes that failing to do so leads to difficulty in establishing sound legal principles.
3
Examine the example: 'a tenth of a tenth'
The common fatwa uses a ratio to determine impurity of water. This rule appears in many fatwa books and is often acted upon.
The passage says 'الفتاوى مملوؤة باعتباره' – the fatwas are filled with it.
4
Contrast with the authentic madhhab
The actual madhhab, as stated by Imam Muhammad in al-Muwatta' and the early companions, depends on whether the water moves from one side when the other is moved. If not, it remains pure.
This shows a clear difference: the authentic ruling is based on physical movement, not a fixed ratio.
5
Understand the consequence
A mufti who does not distinguish will issue a fatwa based on a later derivation, contradicting the genuine madhhab. This undermines the integrity of the school.
The passage warns: 'تعسر عليه تأصيله على أصل شرعي معتمد عليه'.

Source Text

أصول الإفتاء
۱۵۰
طبقات الفقهاء .
الفتاوى المعتبرة المختلفة، كالخلاصة والظهيريّة وفتاوى قاضي خان وغيرها من الفتاوى التى لم يميّز أصحابها بين المذهب والتخريج وغيره، قول أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه، بل منها ما هو منقول عنهم، ومنها ما هو مستنبط الفقها ومنها ما هو مخرج الفقهاء، فيجب على الناظر فيها أن لا يتجاسر على نسبة كل ما فيها إليهم، بل يميز بين ما هو قولهم وبين ما هو مخرج بعدهم. ومن لم يميز بين ذلك وبين هذا أشكل الأمر عليه ألا ترى فى مسئلة العشر في العشر في بحث الحياض، فإن الفتاوى مملوؤة باعتباره، والفتوى عليه، مع أنه ليس مذهب صاحب المذهب، وإنّما مذهبه كما صرح به محمد محمد في الموطأ وقدماء أصحابنا هو أنه لو كان الحوض بحيث لا يتحرك أحد جوانبه بتحريك الجانب الآخر لا يتنجس بوقوع النّجاسة فيه وإلا يتنجس. ومن لم يتفطنه وظنّ أنّه مذهب صاحب المذهب، تعسر عليه تأصيله على أصل شرعي معتمد عليه.
(1)M
ثم ذكر الإمام اللكنوى تقسيماً آخر لمسائل الحنفية بحسب قوة الدليل، وذكر أنه إذا تبين للعالم فى مسألةٍ أن مذهب إمامه يُعارض جديثاً صحيحاً فإنّه يعمل بما وافق الحديث، وبهذا لا يخرحُ عن التقليد. وهذا إنّما يتأتى فيمن يصلح للنظر فى الدلائل وقدمنا شروطها وآدابها في مبحث التقليد. وأمّا المُفتى الحنفي المقلّد الذى لا يستطيع النظر في ذلك يجب عليه أن يلتزم بقواعد رسم المفتى التى شرحها العلامة ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى في شرح عقود رسم المفتى. ونُريد الآن أن نأتي بتلك القواعد بتلخيص وبشيئ من الشرح والإيضاح من مصادر أخرى. والله سبحانه هو الموفق.
(۱) مقدمة النافع الكبير شرح الجامع الصغير ص ١١ و ١٢

تلخيص قواعد رسم المفتى
على مذهب الحنفية
Principles of Issuing Fatwas – 150 – The Layers of Jurists. The various reliable fatwa collections, such as al-Khulasa, al-Zahiriyya, Fatawa Qadi Khan, and other fatwas whose authors did not distinguish between the madhhab and derivation (takhrij) and other [categories] – the statement of Abu Hanifa and his two companions — rather some of them are transmitted from them, some are deduced by the jurists, and some are derived by the jurists. So it is incumbent upon the one who examines them not to dare to attribute everything in them to them, but rather to distinguish between what is their statement and what is a derivation after them. Whoever does not distinguish between this and that will find the matter difficult. Do you not see the issue of 'a tenth of a tenth' in the discussion of water basins? Indeed, the fatwas are filled with considering it, and fatwa is given upon it, even though it is not the madhhab of the founder of the madhhab. Rather his madhhab, as stated by Muhammad in the Muwatta' and the early companions, is that if the basin is such that one of its sides does not move by moving the other side, it does not become impure by the fall of impurity into it; otherwise it becomes impure. Whoever does not grasp this and thinks that it is the madhhab of the founder of the madhhab will find it difficult to base it upon a sound, reliable legal principle.
(1)M
Then Imam al-Laknawi mentioned another classification of Hanafi issues according to the strength of the evidence, and stated that if it becomes clear to a scholar in a matter that the madhhab of his imam contradicts an authentic hadith, he acts in accordance with what agrees with the hadith, and by this he does not leave taqlid. This only applies to one who is qualified to examine the evidences, and we have already presented its conditions and etiquette in the section on taqlid. As for the Hanafi mufti muqallid who cannot examine that, he must adhere to the rules of Rasm al-Mufti which 'Allama Ibn 'Abidin, may Allah have mercy on him, explained in Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. Now we intend to present those rules in summary with some explanation and clarification from other sources. Allah, the Exalted, is the Grantor of success.
(1) Introduction to al-Nafi' al-Kabir Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir, pp. 11-12.

Summary of the Rules of Rasm al-Mufti according to the Hanafi Madhhab
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage is an introduction to the methodology of a Hanafi mufti, emphasizing the critical need to distinguish between the original positions of the founding imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) and later juristic deductions (takhrij) and fatwas. The author warns that many fatwa collections mix these layers, making it essential for the mufti to be discerning. He provides a concrete example from the chapter on impurities in water: the common fatwa on 'a tenth of a tenth' (a ratio for considering water impurity) is widely adopted, but the actual madhhab of Imam Muhammad in the Muwatta' is different, based on the physical movement of water sides. Ignoring this distinction leads to unsound legal foundations. The author then references Imam al-Laknawi's classification of Hanafi issues by evidentiary strength, explaining that a qualified scholar may depart from the madhhab for a strong hadith without abandoning taqlid. However, the ordinary mufti who cannot weigh evidences must follow the rules of Rasm al-Mufti as codified by Ibn 'Abidin. The author promises to present these rules in summary form, drawing from multiple sources.

Key Terms
طبقات الفقهاء (Tabaqat al-Fuqaha'): The hierarchical classification of Hanafi jurists according to their level of authority (e.g., mujtahid, muqallid).
رسم المفتى (Rasm al-Mufti): A set of methodological rules that a mufti must follow when issuing fatwas, especially when the madhhab has multiple positions.
الفتاوى المعتبرة (al-Fatawa al-Mu'tabarah): Reliable fatwa collections used for issuing verdicts, but which may contain later derivations not attributable to the founding imams.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct approach for a Hanafi mufti when using fatwa collections?
A) Rely solely on them because they are widely used.
B) Distinguish between the original madhhab and later derivations.
C) Always follow the ruling that is easier for the people.
D) Ignore them and only use the Qur'an and Sunnah.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi mufti must not blindly accept rulings from later fatwa collections; he must verify each ruling against the authentic transmissions from the founding imams.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
7 min
The Mufti Muqallid and the Obligation of Rasm al-Mufti
Introduction to the obligation of muqallid muftis to follow Rasm al-Mufti and the distinction from qualified scholars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between a scholar who can weigh evidences and a muqallid mufti, and state the obligation of the latter to adhere to the rules of Rasm al-Mufti.

Core Idea
A mufti who cannot independently verify proofs must follow Rasm al-Mufti — the methodology that safeguards the madhhab.

This passage shifts from the warning about fatwa collections to a broader principle: a Hanafi scholar who is capable of evaluating evidences may, under certain conditions, depart from the madhhab when it contradicts a strong hadith. However, the ordinary mufti (muqallid) does not have that luxury. He must stick to the rules of Rasm al-Mufti as codified by later authorities like Ibn 'Abidin. This lesson outlines that distinction and prepares you for the summary of those rules.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two categories
The passage distinguishes between a 'scholar' (al-ʿālim) who is qualified to examine proofs and a 'mufti muqallid' (the Hanafi mufti who follows taqlid).
The scholar may, in specific cases, prefer a hadith over the madhhab; the muqallid cannot.
2
Note the exception for the qualified scholar
Imam al-Laknawi explains that if it becomes clear to a qualified scholar that the madhhab contradicts an authentic hadith, he acts by the hadith. This does not take him out of taqlid.
The conditions and etiquette for this have been discussed earlier in the book.
3
Recognize the rule for the muqallid mufti
The mufti who cannot evaluate proofs (muqallid) must adhere strictly to the rules of Rasm al-Mufti.
This is the core rule for issuing fatwas in the Hanafi school for non-mujtahids.
4
Identify the source of Rasm al-Mufti
The rules were explained by 'Allama Ibn 'Abidin in his commentary on 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti.
This work is a key reference for Hanafi iftaa methodology.
5
Anticipate the summary
The author announces that he will now present these rules in summary with explanation from other sources.
This sets the stage for the subsequent sections of the book.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what must a Hanafi muqallid mufti do when the madhhab appears to contradict a hadith?
A) Follow the hadith because it is stronger.
B) Follow the madhhab because he is bound by taqlid and must adhere to Rasm al-Mufti.
C) Seek the opinion of other scholars.
D) Derive a new ruling from the hadith.

Key Takeaway
A muqallid mufti must not step outside the madhhab; he must adhere to the rules of Rasm al-Mufti, even if he knows a conflicting hadith.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
12 min
Conditions of the Mufti: The First Principle of Rasm al-Mufti
Summarizing the first principle: conditions of the mufti.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five core conditions of a mufti's qualification (ahliyya) and apply the reasoning that male-ness and freedom are not required, citing the analogy to a narrator (rawi).

Core Idea
A mufti needs a faculty (malaka) from study, not just knowledge; male-ness and freedom are not required.

This lesson examines the first principle of the mufti's office: the conditions that qualify a person to issue fatwas. The passage from Mufti Muhammad Taqi Usmani's 'Usul al-Ifta' outlines that mere book-reading is insufficient; a deep faculty (malaka) must be acquired under skilled teachers. We will break down each condition and understand why the mufti's role is akin to a narrator, not a judge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary condition: malaka
Locate where the passage states that giving fatwa is impermissible without first acquiring a malaka (faculty) from study under skilled teachers. Understand that this malaka enables the mufti to grasp principles, rules, and causes, and to distinguish reliable books.
This is the foundational requirement that goes beyond mere knowledge.
2
List the explicit conditions
From the summary: bulugh (puberty), aql (intellect), ilm (knowledge), tajriba (experience), adala (uprightness), and thiqat al-ulama (trust of scholars). Note that ilm here means knowledge acquired through the malaka process.
These conditions are derived from the works of Ibn Abidin and Ibn Hajar al-Haytami.
3
Examine what is NOT required: male-ness and freedom
The passage explicitly states that dhukura (male-ness) and hurriyya (freedom) are not conditions. A woman and a slave may give fatwa if other conditions are met. Understand the evidence from Ibn al-Salah: the mufti is like a narrator (rawi), not a witness or judge.
This is a key distinction from the role of a qadi.
4
Distinguish mufti from judge and narrator
Analyze the reasoning: the mufti informs about Shariah (ikhbar) with no personal interest, and his fatwa is not binding (ilzam). Therefore, he is analogous to a narrator in Hadith, not a witness. This affects which conditions apply.
This analogy justifies the relaxation of conditions like freedom and male-ness.
5
Apply the caution: avoiding accusation
Although the original ruling allows fatwa from a woman or slave, the passage adds a practical note: the mufti should avoid situations of accusation (tuhma). If he fears accusation, he should delegate to another.
This is an adab (etiquette) consideration, not a condition.

Source Text
