الأصل الخامس
يجب على المفتى أن لا يعتمد إلا على الكتب المعتبرة في المذهب ولا يعتمد بأقوال منقولة في كتب غير معتبرة. إن من أهم ما يُشترط للمفتى أن يعرف الكتب المعتمدة من غيرها. والكتب المعتمدة في المذهب هي التي عوّل عليها المتبحرون من أصحاب المذهب، وتناولوها بالثّقة والاعتماد وأفتوا بها، وقد ذكر غير واحد من الفقهاء كتباً لا يجوز الإفتاء بمسائلها ما لم يُعرف مأخذها أو دليلها. وقد عد العلامة ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى منها: شرح النقاية للقهستاني المسمى بجامع الرموز، والدر المختار والأشباه والنظائر، وشرح الكنز لمنلا مسكين، والقِنْية للزاهدي، والنهر الفائق لابن نجيم، وشرح الكنز للعيني.

وضمّ إليها بعضهم السراج الوهاج والجوهرة النيرة شرح القدوري، وكنز العباد في شرح الأوراد لعلي بن أحمد الغَوْرِي، وخزانة الروايات، وخلاصة الكَيْداني، والحاوى للزاهدي، والفتاوى الصوفية، وفتاوى الطُّوري وغيرها.

ولا بد من معرفة وجوه كونها غير معتبرة، وهي متعددة:
الوجه الأول: عدم الاطلاع على حال مؤلفه
ربما يكون الكتاب غير معتبر لعدم معرفة حال المؤلف، فإنّه لا يُعرف هل كان فقيهاً موثوقاً به أم جامعاً للرطب واليابس. فمنها خلاصة الكَيْداني، فإنّه لا يُعرف مؤلّفه، وقد ثبت أنه ذكر فيها روايات واهية، بالرغم من أن الكتاب كان متداولاً في بلاد ما وراء النهر حفظاً وتدريساً. ومنها: خِزانة الروايات، فإنّ مؤلّفَه غير معروف، وقد نسبه صاحب "كشف الظَّنون" إلى قاضي جَكَن الهندي الكجراتي ولا يُعرف حاله. ويوجد فيها أيضاً روايات واهية غير موثوق بها. ومنها كُتب القُهِسْتَانِي، فإنّها وإن تداولها الناس، ولكنه رجل لا يُعرف حاله، وقد جاء في كشف الظنون عن المولى عصام الدين رحمه الله تعالى أنه لم يكن من تلامذة شيخ الإسلام الهروي، وإنما كان دلال الكتب في زمانه
The Fifth Principle: The mufti must rely only on the authoritative books of the madhhab and not rely on statements transmitted in non-authoritative books. One of the most important requirements for a mufti is that he know the authoritative books from others. The authoritative books in the madhhab are those upon which the penetrating scholars of the madhhab relied, and they dealt with them with trust and confidence and issued fatwas from them. Many jurists have mentioned books from which it is not permissible to issue fatwas based on their issues unless their source or evidence is known. Allamah Ibn Abidin (may Allah have mercy on him) counted among them: Sharh al-Niqayah by al-Qahistani called Jami' al-Rumuz, al-Durr al-Mukhtar, al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir, Sharh al-Kanz by Mulla Miskin, al-Qunyah by al-Zahidi, al-Nahr al-Fa'iq by Ibn Nujaym, and Sharh al-Kanz by al-'Ayni. Some added to them al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah sharh al-Quduri, Kanz al-'Ibad fi Sharh al-Awrad by 'Ali ibn Ahmad al-Ghawri, Khizanat al-Riwayat, Khulasat al-Kaydani, al-Hawi by al-Zahidi, al-Fatawa al-Sufiyyah, and Fatawa al-Turi and others. It is necessary to understand the aspects of being non-authoritative, and they are multiple: The first aspect: lack of familiarity with the condition of its author. Perhaps a book is non-authoritative due to not knowing the author's condition, for one does not know whether he was a reliable jurist or a collector of wet and dry. Among them is Khulasat al-Kaydani, for its author is unknown, and it has been confirmed that it contains weak narrations, despite the book being circulated in the lands beyond the river for memorization and teaching. And among them is Khizanat al-Riwayat, for its author is unknown, and the author of Kashf al-Zunun attributed it to Qadi Jakan al-Hindi al-Gujarati, and his condition is unknown. It also contains weak, unreliable narrations. And among them are the books of al-Qahistani, for although people circulated them, he is a man whose condition is unknown. It has come in Kashf al-Zunun from Mawla 'Isam al-Din (may Allah have mercy on him) that he was not among the students of Shaykh al-Islam al-Harawi, but rather he was a bookseller in his time.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Ifta' by Mufti Muhammad Taqi Usmani expounds the fifth principle (al-asl al-khamis) of Rasm al-Mufti: the mufti must rely exclusively on the madhhab's authoritative books. The author explains that authoritative books are those that the madhhab's deeply learned scholars have relied upon, vetted, and used for fatwa. He then lists specific works identified by Ibn Abidin as authoritative: Jami' al-Rumuz (Sharh al-Niqayah by al-Qahistani), al-Durr al-Mukhtar, al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir, Sharh al-Kanz by Mulla Miskin, al-Qunyah, al-Nahr al-Fa'iq, and Sharh al-Kanz by al-'Ayni. Others have added a longer list including al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, and others. The passage then introduces the necessity of recognizing why some books are not considered authoritative. It gives the first of several aspects (later pages continue more aspects): the author's unknown or untrustworthy condition. Three examples: Khulasat al-Kaydani (unknown author, weak narrations), Khizanat al-Riwayat (unknown author, weak narrations), and the books of al-Qahistani (author unknown to be a proper scholar, a bookseller). Despite their popularity, such books cannot be relied upon for fatwa without further verification. The mufti must be discerning and not assume a book's authority based solely on its circulation.

Key Terms
الكتب المعتبرة (al-kutub al-mu'tabara): The books that are reliable and authoritative in the Hanafi madhhab, as determined by the mujtahid scholars of the school.
الوجه الأول (al-wajh al-awwal): The first reason for a book being non-authoritative: lack of knowledge about its author's condition and qualifications.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The book is old and difficult to read.
B) Lack of knowledge about the author's condition and reliability.
C) The book is not included in the list of Ibn Abidin.
D) The book is only used in certain regions.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must only rely on books that the madhhab's scholars have explicitly vetted; popularity does not guarantee authority.

First Reason for Non-Consideration: Unknown Author
Listing additional books and explaining the first reason for non-consideration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the first reason a book is disregarded in Hanafi fatwa methodology and apply it to evaluate the reliability of a given text.

Core Idea
A book's authority in fatwa depends on the trustworthiness of its author, not its popularity.

This passage addresses a key principle in Hanafi fatwa methodology: not all books are equally reliable. The author lists several books that are sometimes added to the canon, then provides the first reason a book may be disregarded: unknown author. Understanding this principle helps a mufti evaluate sources correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the list of books mentioned
The passage begins by stating that some scholars added to the reliable books: al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah, Kanz al-‘Ibad, Khizanat al-Riwayat, Khulasat al-Kaydani, al-Hawi li al-Zahidi, al-Fatawa al-Sufiyya, Fatawa al-Turi, and others.
These are not all of equal reliability; the author will explain which are problematic.
2
Recognize the first reason: unknown author
The first reason a book may be non-considered is lack of knowledge about the author's state: whether he is a trustworthy jurist or not.
This is a fundamental criterion: if the author is unknown, the book cannot be relied upon.
3
Examine the examples given
The author gives four examples: Khulasat al-Kaydani (author unknown, contains weak narrations), Khizanat al-Riwayat (author unknown, weak narrations), books of al-Quhistani (not a student of a known shaykh, was a book dealer, not known for fiqh), and Sharh al-Kanz by Mulla Miskin (author known only as a Hanafi jurist from Herat, but no further details).
Despite circulation, these are unreliable due to unknown or questionable authorship.
4
Understand why authorial authority is critical in Hanafi ifta
In Hanafi usul al-ifta, the reliability of a book depends on the author's knowledge, piety, and trustworthiness. If the author is unknown, the book's contents may contain weak or fabricated narrations, so it cannot be used for fatwa.
This principle ensures that only sound, well-sourced rulings are issued.

Commentary
This passage is a methodological rule from the Hanafi fatwa tradition, specifically from the section 'Talkhis Qawa'id Rasm al-Mufti.' It begins by listing additional books that some scholars include among the reliable sources for fatwa, such as al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and others. Then it introduces the first reason why a book may not be considered reliable: lack of knowledge about the author's scholarly standing. The author explains that if the author's reliability is unknown, the book cannot be trusted. He gives several examples: Khulasat al-Kaydani, whose author is unknown and contains weak narrations; Khizanat al-Riwayat, also of unknown authorship and containing weak narrations; the books of al-Quhistani, whose author was a book dealer and not known for fiqh; and Sharh al-Kanz by Mulla Miskin, again of unknown status. The passage includes footnotes clarifying the identity of Shaykh al-Islam al-Harawi (the grandson of Sa‘d al-Din al-Taftazani). The reason is clear: a book's authority depends on the author's trustworthiness in the madhhab. This is a foundational principle in Hanafi usul al-ifta.

Key Terms
الوجه الأول: عدم الاطلاع على حال مؤلفه (al-wajh al-awwal: ‘adam al-ittila‘ ‘ala hal mu’allifihi): The first reason a book is deemed unreliable: lack of knowledge about the author's scholarly standing and trustworthiness.
خلاصة الكَيْداني (Khulasat al-Kaydani): A book whose author is unknown; contains weak narrations despite being widely circulated in Transoxiana.
خزانة الروايات (Khizanat al-Riwayat): Another book with unknown author and weak narrations, mentioned as an example of an unreliable text.
كتب القُهسْتَانِي (Kutub al-Quhistani): Books by al-Quhistani, whose author was a book dealer not known for fiqh, thus unreliable.
شرح الكنز لملاً مسكين (Sharh al-Kanz li-Mulla Miskin): A commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq by Mulla Miskin, a Hanafi jurist from Herat, but his full status is unknown.

D) It was never formally taught in madrasas.

Key Takeaway
A book's reliability for Hanafi fatwa hinges on the known trustworthiness of its author, not on its popularity or circulation.

Second Reason for Non-Consideration: Weak Narrations
Explaining the second reason a book may be disregarded: author compiled weak narrations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a book is non-considered due to weak narrations and apply this principle to evaluate sources in fatwa.

Core Idea
Even a reputable scholar's book loses authority if he transmits weak narrations without scrutiny.

In Hanafi fatwa methodology, not every book by a renowned jurist is automatically reliable. The second reason a book may be disregarded is that its author, despite his scholarship, compiled weak narrations without verification. This lesson examines this principle through the example of al-Qunyah by al-Zahidi.

Guided Path
1
State the rule
Identify the second reason a book is non-considered: the author compiled weak narrations.
The passage explicitly gives this as 'al-wajh al-thani'.
2
Understand the rationale
Explain why weak narrations reduce a book's authority: the author did not restrict himself to authentic narrations but transmitted everything without scrutiny.
This reflects the Hanafi emphasis on textual authenticity.
3
Apply to the example
Analyze the case of al-Qunyah: its author, al-Zahidi, was a great jurist but 'mutasahil fi naql al-riwayat' (lenient in transmitting narrations).
Shaykh al-Lakhnawi's statement is key: 'despite his majesty, he was lenient.'
4
Distinguish from reliable works
Contrast this with books where the author carefully selected only authentic narrations, like the works of Zahir al-Riwayah.
This distinction is crucial for a mufti's source hierarchy.
5
Conclude for practice
A mufti should not rely on a book just because its author is famous; he must examine the author's method of narration.
This is a key nuance in usul al-iftaa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الثاني : جمع المؤلف روايات ضعيفة الوجه الثاني في كون الكتاب غير معتبر : أن يجمع مؤلفه روايات ضعيفة. وحاصله أن مؤلفي هذه الكتب، وإن كانوا معروفين بالعلم والفقه، ولكنهم لم يلتزموا في هذه الكتب بالاقتصار علي الروايات الصحيحة، بل نقلوا كل ما وجدوا من قول أو رواية من غير تحقيق أو تنقيح. فمنها: القنية للزاهدي: فإنّ مؤلفه مختار بن محمود بن محمد أبو الرجاء نجم الدين الزاهدي معروف بكونه عالماً، وهو معتزلي الإعتقاد حنفي الفروع، كان من غزمين قصبة من قصبات خوارزم. وقال الشيخ اللّكنوي رحمه الله تعالى: "كان من كبار الأئمة وأعيان الفقهاء.... وهو مع جلالته متساهل في نقل الروايات." و قد ذكر قبل كل مسئلة رمزاً لمأخذ تلك المسألة، وقد شرح الرموز في مقدمة كتابه.
: وكان رحمه الله رئيس العلماء بهراة وقاضيها لثلاثين عاماً، ولما دخلها الشاه إسماعيل بن حيدر الصفوي كان الحفيد ممن جلسوا لاستقباله فى دار الإمارة، ولكن الوشاة الهموه عند الشاه بالتعصب، فأمر بقتله فاستشهد مع جماعة من علماء هراة ، ولم يُعرف له ذنب، ونُعِت بالشهيد. من تصانيفه الفقهية: تعليقة على أوائل الهداية، وحاشية على شرح الوقاية، وشرح فرائض السراجية (ملخص) من الأعلام ۱ : ۲۷۰ وهدية العارفين ۱: ۱۳۸ و ۲ (۵۲۹ (1) الأعلام للزركلى ٦:٢٣٧
The second aspect: the author compiled weak narrations. The second aspect of a book being non-considered is that its author compiled weak narrations. The summary is that the authors of these books, although they were known for knowledge and fiqh, did not restrict themselves in these books to authentic narrations, but rather transmitted every statement or narration they found without verification or scrutiny. Among them is al-Qunyah for al-Zahidi: its author is Mukhtar ibn Mahmud ibn Muhammad Abu al-Raja’ Najm al-Din al-Zahidi, known for being a scholar, and he was a Mu’tazili in creed, Hanafi in branches. He was from Ghazmin, a district of Khwarazm. Shaykh al-Lakhnawi, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'He was among the great imams and notable jurists... and despite his majesty, he was lenient in transmitting narrations.' And he mentioned before every issue a symbol for the source of that issue, and he explained the symbols in the introduction to his book. (Footnote): And he, may Allah have mercy on him, was the chief of scholars in Herat and its judge for thirty years. When Shah Isma‘il ibn Haydar al-Safawi entered it, al-Hafid was among those who sat to receive him in the governor's residence, but the slanderers incited the Shah against him on grounds of partisanship, so he ordered his execution, and he was martyred with a group of scholars of Herat. No sin was known of him, and he was called al-Shahid (the martyr). Among his juristic works: a gloss on the beginning of al-Hidayah, a marginalia on Sharh al-Wiqayah, and a commentary on Fara’id al-Sirajiyyah (summarized) from al-A‘lam 1:270, Hadiyyat al-‘Arifin 1:138 and 2 (529), and al-A‘lam by al-Zirikli 6:237.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage presents the second reason why a book may not be considered reliable in Hanafi fatwa methodology: the author, though himself a known scholar, compiled weak narrations without proper scrutiny. The author notes that these authors did not limit themselves to authentic narrations but transmitted everything they found. The primary example given is al-Qunyah by al-Zahidi. Despite al-Zahidi being a recognized jurist (though Mu‘tazili in creed), he was lenient in transmitting narrations, as stated by Shaykh ‘Abd al-Hayy al-Lakhnawi. The passage then includes a footnote about al-Hafid (the grandson of al-Taftazani), detailing his scholarly stature and martyrdom in Herat. The key point for the mufti is that a known scholar's name does not guarantee the reliability of every book he authored; the content must be critically evaluated for adherence to authentic transmissions. This is a crucial nuance in Hanafi usul al-iftaa.

Key Terms
القنية للزاهدي (al-Qunyah li al-Zahidi): A book by al-Zahidi; considered unreliable for fatwa because it contains weak narrations despite the author's knowledge.
الوجه الثاني: جمع المؤلف روايات ضعيفة (al-wajh al-thani: jam‘ al-mu’allif riwayat da‘ifah): The second reason a book is non-considered: the author compiled weak narrations without verification.

Checkpoint
Why is al-Qunyah by al-Zahidi considered unreliable according to the second reason?
A) Because its author was not a Hanafi in fiqh.
B) Because the author was lenient in transmitting narrations and did not restrict himself to authentic ones.
C) Because the book was written after the author's death.
D) Because it was banned by the Safavid authorities.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must evaluate a book's reliability not by the author's fame but by his method of narration; weak narrations in a book render it non-considered for fatwa.

Critiquing Fatwa Sources: The Case of al-Zahidi and al-Muhit al-Burhani
Critiquing al-Zahidi and al-Muhit for fatwa reliability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the reliability of Hanafi fatwa sources by applying the criteria of weak narrations, author's creed, and scholarly consensus.

Core Idea
A mufti may not issue fatwa from a book containing weak narrations or deviant beliefs, regardless of the author's reputation.

This passage from Rasm al-Mufti addresses a critical skill for the mufti: distinguishing reliable from unreliable sources. Using the example of al-Zahidi's works and the Muhit al-Burhani, the author demonstrates that even respected Hanafi scholars can produce texts that are not fit for fatwa. This lesson will guide you through the reasoning behind these evaluations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source under scrutiny
In this passage, two sets of works are examined: those of al-Zahidi (al-Quniya and al-Hawi) and the Muhit al-Burhani. Note the names and why they are being discussed.
Al-Zahidi is a Hanafi scholar, but his books are criticized for weak narrations and Mu'tazili tendencies.
2
Examine the criticism: weak narrations
The passage cites a specific example: al-Zahidi's ruling that kohl must be abandoned on Ashura. Al-Tahawi rejects this because al-Quniya is not among the reliable books. Identify the basis of the criticism: the hadith or report is weak.
Weak narrations are a common flaw; a mufti must verify the strength of the evidence.
3
Examine the criticism: author's creed (i'tizal)
Al-Zahidi's deviation is exposed in the issue of gifting reward (ihda' al-thawab). He contradicts al-Hidayah and adopts a Mu'tazili view. Al-Haskafi and Ibn Abidin highlight this as a sign of his doctrinal error.
I'tizal affects the reliability of a scholar's legal opinions, especially when they contradict the majority.
4
Analyze the scholarly response to al-Muhit
Later scholars like Ibn Nujaym and Ibn Humam forbade fatwa from al-Muhit, calling it 'dry and wet' (mixed). But al-Lakhnawi later defended it after careful study, showing that blanket rejections may be reconsidered.
This demonstrates that evaluations can change with deeper analysis; but the default is caution.
5
Synthesize the fatwa hierarchy principle
From these examples, formulate the rule: a book is reliable for fatwa if its narrations are strong, its author adheres to the madhhab's usul, and it is accepted by the majority of later scholars. Individual opinions that conflict with the mainstream are not authoritative.
This aligns with the Hanafi principle of relying on the mufta bihi (operative opinion) from established sources.

Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage discusses the criteria for determining which books are reliable for issuing fatwas. It begins by noting that some books contain strange or unreliable narrations, using al-Zahidi's works as examples. Al-Tahawi and Ibn Wahban caution against relying on al-Quniya and al-Hawi due to their inclusion of weak narrations. The passage then highlights a specific case where al-Zahidi deviated from the majority Hanafi position on the permissibility of gifting reward (ihda' al-thawab), aligning instead with a Mu'tazili view. This illustrates that even a scholar's personal creed can affect his legal rulings, and such deviations must be identified. The discussion then shifts to al-Muhit al-Burhani, a celebrated Hanafi work. While its author was a capable scholar, some later authorities forbade giving fatwa from it due to its mixed reliability. However, al-Lakhnawi later defended it after careful study, suggesting that blanket rejections may be reconsidered. The overall lesson is that muftis must exercise critical judgment regarding their sources, not blindly accepting any book attributed to the madhhab.

Key Terms
القنية (al-Quniya): A book by al-Zahidi containing fatwas, but considered unreliable by later scholars due to weak narrations.
الحاوي (al-Hawi): Another work by al-Zahidi, similarly criticized for transmitting weak narrations.
الزاهدي (al-Zahidi): A Hanafi scholar whose books contain weak narrations and some deviant views (i'tizal), making him unreliable for fatwa when he contradicts established authorities.
إهداء الثواب (ihda' al-thawab): Gifting the spiritual reward of one's acts of worship to another person, living or deceased.
المحيط البرهاني (al-Muhit al-Burhani): A comprehensive Hanafi fiqh work by Imam Burhan al-Din al-Bukhari; its reliability for fatwa is debated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Ibn Abidin reject al-Zahidi's ruling on kohl on the day of Ashura?
A) Because al-Zahidi was not a reliable narrator of hadith.
B) Because the ruling was based on a weak narration transmitted in al-Quniya.
C) Because the ruling contradicted the Quran.
D) Because al-Zahidi was a Mu'tazili.

Key Takeaway
Reliability for fatwa depends on the strength of narrations and adherence to the madhhab's usul, not merely the author's fame.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Evaluating Books for Fatwa: Al-Muhit al-Burhani's Rehabilitation
Refining scholarly evaluation of al-Muhit al-Burhani for fatwa use

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a book's authority for fatwa can change with its availability and scholarly verification, using the case of al-Muhit al-Burhani.

Core Idea
A book's scarcity, not its content, may cause its rejection; later verification revives its authority.

When you encounter a historical prohibition on a fiqh book, it's tempting to dismiss it forever. But this lesson reveals a deeper principle: context matters. The case of al-Muhit al-Burhani shows that a book once deemed unfit for fatwa can become a primary source once it is available and its contents are properly assessed. You'll learn to distinguish between content-based rejections and circumstantial ones.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Book and the Historical Claim
Find the book mentioned—al-Muhit al-Burhani—and note the early scholars' ruling: they prohibited giving fatwa from it. Some said it mixed sound and weak material.
The early jurists were Ibn Nujaym and Ibn Humam.
2
Analyze the Reason for Prohibition
Al-Lakhnawi investigated and found the book well-organized, not a mix. He concluded the prohibition was due to its rarity (naadir al-wujud), not content flaws.
This is the key turning point in the passage.
3
Apply the Principle of Changed Circumstances
The author notes that the book is now printed and critically edited. Therefore, the earlier prohibition no longer applies. Availability and scholarly verification can elevate a book's status.
Think: 'This ruling varies with time.'
4
Determine the Current Mufta Bihi
The passage concludes that al-Muhit al-Burhani should be considered a reliable primary source (ummahat al-kutub al-mu'tabara), with clear separation of Zahir al-Riwaya and Nawadir.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.
5
Generalize the Rule for Other Books
Apply this lesson to other books listed at the end: books like 'Kanz al-Abbad' are inherently unreliable (filled with weak material), so they remain in the prohibited category regardless of availability.
The principle: distinguish between circumstantial and substantive rejection.

تلخيص قواعد رسم المفتي

فلما ذكر الحصكفي رحمه الله تعالى مسئلة إهداء الثواب، قال: "ولقد أفصح الزاهدي عن اعتزاله هنا." وقال ابن عابدين تحته: "حيث قال في المجتبى بعد ذكره عبارة الهداية: قلت: ومذهب أهل العدل والتوحيد أنه ليس له ذلك الخ" فعدل عن الهداية، وسمّى أهل عقيدته بأهل العدل والتوحيد لقولهم بوجوب الأصلح على الله تعالى وأنه لو لم يفعل ذلك، لكان جوراً منه تعالى. والعياذ بالله من ذلك. وقد عد العلماء المتأخرون "المحيط البرهاني" فإن مؤلّفه من أعيان العلماء الحنفية، حتى انه من المجتهدين في المسائل، ولكن نص الفقهاء كابن نجيم وابن همام بأنه لا يجوز الإفتاء به، وعلله بعضهم بكونه جامعاً للرطب واليابس، ولكن ذكر العلامة اللكنوي رحمه الله تعالى هذا الكلام من هؤلاء العلماء، ثمّ كتب في حاشية النافع الكبير ما نصه: "وقد وفقني الله بعد كتابة هذه الرسالة بمطالعة المحيط البرهاني، فرأيتُه ليس جامعاً للرطب واليابس، بل فيه مسائل منقحة وتفاريع مرصصة، ثمّ تأملت في عبارة فتح القدير وعبارة ابن نجيم، فعلمت أن المنع من الإفتاء منه ليس لكونه جامعاً للغث والسمين، بل لكونه مفقوداً نادر الوجود في ذلك العصر. وهذا الأمر يختلف باختلاف الزمان." وعليه، فذكره الفقهاء المتأخرون فى جملة الكتب التي لا يفتى بها لكونه من القسم الرابع الآتى، لا في هذا القسم. ولكن قد طُبع هذا الكتاب اليوم بفضل الله تعالى في خمسة وعشرين مجلداً، وقد حققه ابن أختى الفاضل الشيخ نعيم أشرف حفظه الله تعالى بمقابلة عدة نُسخ خطيّة حصل عليها من مكتبات متفرقة، وقد طالعت منه قدراً يُعتد به، وإنّه ذكر في جميع الأبواب مسائل ظاهر الرواية، ثمّ مسائل النوادر، ثمّ النوازل والفتاوى بترتيب جيد، فلا يمكن القول بأنه خلط بين الرطب واليابس. نعم! توجد فيها روايات النوادر ولكنها ممتازة كل الامتياز عن ظاهر الرواية، فيُطبّق عليها ماذكرنا من أحكام النوادر، دون أن يقع أى التباس أو اشتباه فينبغى أن يُعد هذا الكتاب من أمهات الكتب المعتبرة.

ومنها: "كنز العباد في شرح الأوراد" لعلي بن أحمد الغوري: فإنّه مملوء من مسائل واهية و أحاديث موضوعةٍ لا عبرة لها عند الفقهاء ولا عند المحدثين. وكذلك يندرج في هذا القسم "مطالب المؤمنين" و"الفتاوي الصوفية" و "فتاوي الطوري" وفتاوي ابن نجيم كما ذكره العلامة اللكنوي رحمه الله تعالى في "النافع الكبير". وحكم هذين القسمين أن لا يؤخذ منها ما كان مخالفاً للكتب المعتمدة.
Summary of the Rules of the Mufti's Guide

When al-Haskafi (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned the issue of gifting reward, he said: "Indeed al-Zahidi clearly stated his i'tizal (rejection) here." And Ibn Abidin commented underneath: "He said in al-Mujtaba after mentioning the statement of al-Hidayah: I said: The school of Ahl al-Adl wa al-Tawhid (people of justice and monotheism) is that it is not permissible for him, etc." So he deviated from al-Hidayah, and called the people of his creed "Ahl al-Adl wa al-Tawhid" due to their saying that it is obligatory upon Allah to do what is most beneficial and that if He did not do that, it would be injustice from Him, may He be exalted. We seek refuge in Allah from that.

The later scholars counted "al-Muhit al-Burhani" as [one of the books], for its author is among the notable Hanafi scholars, to the point that he is among the mujtahids in questions. However, the jurists like Ibn Nujaym and Ibn Humam explicitly stated that it is not permissible to give fatwa from it, and some of them explained that it is because it collects the wet and the dry (i.e., mixes sound and weak material). But Allamah al-Lakhnawi (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned this statement from these scholars, then he wrote in his gloss on al-Nafi' al-Kabir the following: "Allah granted me success after writing this treatise to study al-Muhit al-Burhani, and I found it not a collection of wet and dry, rather it contains refined issues and well-structured branches. Then I pondered the statements of Fath al-Qadir and the statement of Ibn Nujaym, and I realized that the prohibition of giving fatwa from it is not because it mixes the thin and the fat, but because it was rare and unavailable in that era. And this matter varies with the variation of time." Therefore, the later jurists mentioned it among the books from which fatwa is not given because it belongs to the fourth category [to be mentioned later], not in this category.

However, this book has been printed today by the grace of Allah in twenty-five volumes, and it has been edited by my nephew, the virtuous Shaykh Na'eem Ashraf (may Allah preserve him), by comparing several handwritten copies he obtained from various libraries. I have reviewed a considerable amount of it, and he mentioned in all chapters the issues of Zahir al-Riwaya, then the issues of Nawadir, then the Nawazil and Fatawa in a good order. So it cannot be said that he mixed the wet and the dry. Yes! There are Nawadir narrations in it, but they are entirely distinct from Zahir al-Riwaya, so the rules we mentioned for Nawadir apply to them without any confusion or ambiguity. Therefore, this book should be considered among the reliable primary sources.

Among [the books in the fourth category] is "Kanz al-Abbad fi Sharh al-Awrad" by Ali ibn Ahmad al-Ghawri: it is filled with weak issues and fabricated hadiths that have no weight with jurists or hadith scholars. Similarly, falling into this category are "Matalib al-Mu'minin", "al-Fatawa al-Sufiyya", "Fatawa al-Turi", and Fatawa Ibn Nujaym as mentioned by Allamah al-Lakhnawi in "al-Nafi' al-Kabir". The ruling for these two categories is that nothing should be taken from them that contradicts the relied-upon books.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage, from the 'Summary of the Rules of the Mufti's Guide', is a critical refinement of the classification of Hanafi fiqh books for issuing fatwas. The author, Muhammad Taqi Usmani, begins by recounting a tangential discussion about al-Haskafi and Ibn Abidin regarding a theological deviation, then moves to the main issue: the status of 'al-Muhit al-Burhani'. The earlier jurists like Ibn Nujaym and Ibn Humam had prohibited issuing fatwa from this book, with some saying it mixed sound and weak material (i.e., it was unreliable). However, Allamah al-Lakhnawi, a later authority, examined the book and found it to be well-organized, containing refined issues and clear distinctions between Zahir al-Riwaya (authoritative transmissions) and Nawadir (rare transmissions). He realized that the prohibition was not due to content but because the book was rare and unavailable in that era. Usmani then notes that today, the book has been printed in a critical edition and is readily available; therefore it should be considered a reliable primary source. He emphasizes that the book clearly separates Zahir al-Riwaya from Nawadir, so there is no confusion. The lesson for the mufti is that the evaluation of a book can change with time and availability. The passage then lists books that are inherently unreliable, such as 'Kanz al-Abbad fi Sharh al-Awrad', and notes that they fall into the fourth category of books from which contradictory material should not be taken. The overarching principle: a mufti must rely on authoritative works, but must also consider historical context and scholarly verification.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwaya): The primary, well-known, and authoritative transmissions of the Hanafi school, primarily from the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
نوادر (Nawadir): Rare or less widely transmitted narrations within the Hanafi school, often from later sources or individual imams like Hasan ibn Ziyad.
المحيط البرهاني (al-Muhit al-Burhani): A comprehensive Hanafi fiqh work by Burhan al-Din al-Bukhari, which was initially considered unreliable by some scholars due to its rarity but later rehabilitated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did al-Lakhnawi discover about al-Muhit al-Burhani after studying it?
A) It is a collection of weak and fabricated hadiths.
B) It is well-organized, with refined issues and clear distinctions between Zahir al-Riwaya and Nawadir.
C) It should be burned because of its author's creed.
D) It only contains Nawadir and no Zahir al-Riwaya.

Key Takeaway
A book's authority for fatwa is not static; it can change with availability and scholarly verification, as demonstrated by the rehabilitation of al-Muhit al-Burhani.

Ruling on Books with Mixed Content for Fatwa
Ruling on books mixing reliable and unreliable content for fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rasm al-mufti rule to evaluate whether a book containing both reliable and unreliable content can be used for fatwa.

Core Idea
A book mixing reliable and weak narrations is rejected if it contradicts reliable works; unique content is suspended.

Not every book that includes weak material is automatically unusable for fatwa. The later Hanafi masters divided books into categories, and this lesson examines the ruling for those that contain both 'al-ghathth' (weak) and 'al-sameen' (sound). The key is to compare with the authoritative books of the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category of the book
Determine whether the book is from Zahir al-Riwayah, Nawadir, or later compilations. The passage discusses books that mix these categories.
Books that clearly separate Zahir al-Riwayah from Nawadir can still be reliable.
2
Check for contradiction with reliable works
Any ruling in the book that contradicts a well-established book from Zahir al-Riwayah must be rejected. The reliable works hold precedence.
The phrase 'الكتب المعتمدة' refers to the core Hanafi texts.
3
Handle unique content not found elsewhere
If the book contains a ruling not found in any reliable book, it is suspended (mutawaqqaf). Investigate whether it fits a valid legal principle and does not conflict with any juristic principle.
This is the default position for such isolated narrations.
4
Apply the ruling on acceptance or rejection
If the unique ruling is consistent with a valid principle and does not oppose a juristic principle, it may be accepted. Otherwise, it is rejected and cannot be used for fatwa.
This balances caution with the possibility of valid rare transmissions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من الإفتاء منه ليس لكونه جامعاً للغث والسمين، بل لكونه مفقوداً نادر الوجود في ذلك العصر. وهذا الأمر يختلف باختلاف الزمان." وعليه، فذكره الفقهاء المتأخرون فى جملة الكتب التي لا يفتى بها لكونه من القسم الرابع الآتى، لا في هذا القسم. ولكن قد طُبع هذا الكتاب اليوم بفضل الله تعالى في خمسة وعشرين مجلداً، وقد حققه ابن أختى الفاضل الشيخ نعيم أشرف حفظه الله تعالى بمقابلة عدة نُسخ خطيّة حصل عليها من مكتبات متفرقة، وقد طالعت منه قدراً يُعتد به، وإنّه ذكر في جميع الأبواب مسائل ظاهر الرواية، ثمّ مسائل النوادر، ثمّ النوازل والفتاوى بترتيب جيد، فلا يمكن القول بأنه خلط بين الرطب واليابس. نعم! توجد فيها روايات النوادر ولكنها ممتازة كل الامتياز عن ظاهر الرواية، فيُطبّق عليها ماذكرنا من أحكام النوادر، دون أن يقع أى التباس أو اشتباه فينبغى أن يُعد هذا الكتاب من أمهات الكتب المعتبرة.
ومنها: "كنز" العبّاد في شرح الأوراد ( لعلي بن أحمد الغَوْرِي: فإنّه مملوء من مسائل واهية و أحاديث موضوعةٍ لا عبرة لها عند الفقهاء ولا عند المحدثين. وكذلك يندرج في هذا القسم "مطالب المؤمنين" و"الفتاوي الصوفية" و "فتاوي الطُّوري" وفتاوي ابن نجيم كما ذكره العلامة اللكنوي رحمه الله تعالى في "النافع الكبير" وحكم هذين القسمين أن لا يؤخذ منها ما كان مخالفاً للكتب المعتمدة،
(1) ورد في كشف الظنون ٢:١٥١٧ أنه مجموعة أوراد الشيخ شهاب الدين السهروردي رحمه الله تعالى والشرح لبعض المشايخ فى مجلد منقول من كتب الفتاوى والواقعات، وهو شرح فارسي لعلى بن أحمد الغوري.
فأما ما وجد فيها ولم يوجد في غيرها، فيُتوقف فيه، فإن دخل ذلك في أصل شرعي، ولم يخالف أصلاً فقهيّاً، فلا بأس بالأخذ به، وإن لم يدخل لم يجز الأخذ أو الإفتاء به.
Some do not issue fatwa from it not because it contains the worthless and the valuable, but because it was missing and rarely found in that era. And this matter differs according to time. Accordingly, the later jurists mentioned it among the books from which fatwa is not issued because it falls under the fourth category to come, not in this category. But today this book has been printed by the grace of Allah in twenty-five volumes, and it has been verified by the son of my sister, the virtuous Shaykh Na'eem Ashraf, may Allah preserve him, by comparing several manuscript copies he obtained from various libraries, and I have read a considerable portion of it. Indeed, he mentioned in all chapters the issues of Zahir al-Riwayah, then the issues of Nawadir, then the Nawazil and Fatawa in a good order, so it cannot be said that he mixed the wet and the dry. Yes, there are narrations of Nawadir in it, but they are completely distinct from Zahir al-Riwayah, so the rulings we mentioned regarding Nawadir apply to them without any confusion or doubt. Therefore, this book should be considered among the reliable primary sources. Among them is "Kanz al-'Ubbad fi Sharh al-Awrad" by Ali ibn Ahmad al-Ghawri: it is filled with weak issues and fabricated hadiths, which carry no weight with the jurists or the hadith scholars. Similarly, included in this section are "Matalib al-Mu'minin", "al-Fatawa al-Sufiyya", "Fatawa al-Turi", and "Fatawa Ibn Nujaym" as mentioned by 'Allama al-Laknawi in "al-Nafi' al-Kabir". The ruling for these two sections is that one should not take from them what contradicts the reliable books. As for what is found in them and not found elsewhere, it is suspended. If it falls under a valid legal principle and does not conflict with a juristic principle, then there is no harm in adopting it; otherwise, it is not permissible to adopt or issue fatwa from it.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti ruling on the categories of books from which fatwa should not be given. The author begins by discussing a particular book that was previously considered lost and thus not used for fatwa, but which has now been published and verified. He explains that the book is actually well-organized, clearly distinguishing Zahir al-Riwayah from Nawadir, so it cannot be accused of mixing reliable and unreliable content. He then mentions several books that are unreliable due to containing weak issues and fabricated hadiths, such as 'Kanz al-'Ubbad', 'Matalib al-Mu'minin', etc. The general ruling for these books is that any content contradicting established reliable works must be rejected. Content unique to these books is to be suspended: if it is based on a valid legal principle and does not conflict with any juristic principle, it may be accepted; otherwise, it cannot be accepted or used for fatwa.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The primary and most authoritative narrations in the Hanafi school, transmitted by Imam Muhammad in six core books.
النوادر (al-Nawadir): Rare transmissions from Hanafi imams, not part of the six core books of Zahir al-Riwayah.
الكتب المعتمدة (al-kutub al-mu'tamada): The reliable books of the Hanafi school that are accepted as authoritative for fatwa.
الغث والسمين (al-ghathth wa al-sameen): A metaphor for weak and strong content in books; 'غث' refers to weak, unreliable material, and 'سمين' to valuable, authentic material.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is suspended and examined: if it aligns with a valid legal principle and does not conflict with juristic principles, it may be accepted.
C) It is accepted without question.

Key Takeaway
A book containing mixed content is not automatically unreliable; the key is whether its rulings contradict established reliable works and, for unique rulings, whether they align with valid legal principles.

Third Category: Excessive Conciseness in Fatwa Books
Explaining that highly respected concise books require commentary for fatwa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify books with excessive conciseness and apply the rule that fatwa is only allowed after reviewing their commentaries.

Core Idea
Concise books are reliable but fatwa requires deep reflection and commentary review.

Not all respected books can be used directly for fatwa. Some are so concise that they risk misunderstanding. This lesson teaches you how to handle such texts—by consulting commentaries and exercising caution—while still recognizing their value.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
Recognize that books like Al-Durr al-Mukhtar and Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir belong to the category of 'excessive conciseness' (ikhtisar mukhll).
These books are authoritative but require careful handling.
2
Understand the ruling
The ruling is that fatwa is not permissible from such books directly. You must first engage in deep reflection (nazar gha'ir) and review their commentaries and glosses.
Even after review, certainty is required before issuing a fatwa.
3
Learn the exceptional caution
Ibn 'Abidin noted that these books may contain transmission errors or unusual preferences, placing them partly in the second category (books not to be followed).
This adds an extra layer of caution: do not assume every statement in them is the relied-upon opinion.
4
Apply the method
When encountering a concise text, always cross-check with its major commentaries (e.g., Radd al-Muhtar for Al-Durr al-Mukhtar) and verify the mufta bihi position.
This ensures your fatwa aligns with the soundest opinion of the madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الثالث: الاختصار المُخل بالفهم.
إنّ هناك كتباً لا شك في جلالة قدرها والثّقة علي مؤلّفيها، ولكن يوجد فيها إيجاز مخل بالفهم، ولذلك قال العلماء: إنه لا يجوز الإفتاء منها، كالدر المختار ، والأشباه والنظائر وغيرها من الكتب الموجزة، ولكن ليس معناه أنّ هذه الكتب غير معتبرة فى نفسها، ولكنّها لما فيها من الإيجاز لا يأمن المفتى من الوقوع في الغلط إذا اقتصر عليها. وحكم هذا القسم أن لا يُفتى منها إلا بعد نظر غائر و فکر دائر و مراجعة شروحها و حواشيها، فإن تيقن المفتي بعد ادها، فلا بأس حينئذ بالإفتاء منها. وقد ذكر العلامة ابن عابدين بمرا رحمه الله في شرح عقود رسم المفتى أنّ الدر المختار والأشباه والنظائر تشتمل علي سقط فى النقل في مواضع كثيرة، و ترجيح ما هو خلاف الراجح، بل ترجيح ما هو مذهب الغير ممّا لم يقل به أحد من أهل المذهب وعلى هذا، فإنّ هذه الكتب داخلة في القسم الثاني أيضاً. (۱)
The third aspect: Excessive conciseness that impedes understanding. There are books whose greatness and reliability of their authors are unquestionable, but they contain conciseness that impedes understanding, and therefore the scholars said: It is not permissible to issue fatwa from them, such as al-Durr al-Mukhtar, al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir, and other concise books. But this does not mean that these books themselves are not reliable; rather, due to their conciseness, the mufti is not safe from falling into error if he relies solely on them. The ruling for this category is that fatwa is not given from them except after deep reflection, thorough consideration, and reviewing their commentaries and glosses. If the mufti becomes certain after that, then there is no harm in issuing fatwa from them. And 'Allama Ibn 'Abidin [al-Mara] mentioned in Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti that al-Durr al-Mukhtar and al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir contain gaps in transmission in many places, and the preference of what is contrary to the relied-upon opinion, even the preference of the view of another school which no one from the Hanafi school has held. Based on this, these books are also included in the second category.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage presents the third ruling (wajh) in the classification of books for fatwa. It addresses books that are highly respected but written in a very concise style, like 'al-Durr al-Mukhtar' and 'al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir', which can lead to misunderstanding if taken alone. The ruling is that such books should not be used for fatwa without consulting their commentaries and glosses to avoid error. Additionally, Ibn 'Abidin notes that these books may contain transmission errors and unusual preferences, placing them partly in the second category (books not to be followed). However, the primary ruling is that they can be used after careful study.

Key Terms
الاختصار المُخل (al-ikhtisar al-mukhalla): Excessive conciseness that leads to ambiguity or misunderstanding, making the text insufficient for fatwa without further explanation.
الدر المختار (Al-Durr al-Mukhtar): A famous Hanafi fiqh book by Haskafi, known for its conciseness.
الأشباه والنظائر (Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir): A work by Ibn Nujaym on Hanafi legal maxims, also concise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is absolutely prohibited.
B) It is permissible only after deep reflection and consulting commentaries.
C) It is permissible without any conditions.
D) It is only allowed for advanced scholars.

Key Takeaway
Concise Hanafi texts like Al-Durr al-Mukhtar require careful study with commentaries; fatwa is not permitted from them without verification.

The Ruling on Rare and Out-of-Print Books in Ifta
Explaining the fourth category of books not to be relied upon

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the fourth category of books requiring caution in ifta and apply the principle of verifying authority before reliance.

Core Idea
A rare book's authority must be proven by strong evidence before it is relied upon for fatwa.

A mufti often encounters books that were authoritative in the past but are now rare or out of print. This lesson examines the fourth category of books that require caution: those whose copies are scarce. The ruling, as conveyed by classical Hanafi scholarship, is not to reject them outright but to verify their authority through compelling proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
Recognize that the book belongs to the fourth category: rare and out-of-print books.
2
Apply the principle of caution
Do not hastily rely on the book; wait for strong evidence of its authority.
The text says 'لا يتعجل' – not to be hasty.
3
Seek strong evidence
Look for evidence such as citation by reliable later scholars, consistent transmission, or verification of the text.
The phrase 'بالدلائل القوية' indicates the need for strong proofs.
4
Determine reliance
Once the evidence is found, the book can be relied upon. If not, it remains questionable.

Explicit and Implicit Tarjih in Hanafi Fatwa Methodology
Defines two types of tarjih and their hierarchy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify two types of tarjih (explicit and implicit) in a Hanafi text and apply the rule that explicit tarjih takes precedence over implicit tarjih when both are present.

Core Idea
Explicit tarjih (clear preference words) always outranks implicit tarjih (inferred from practice) when both exist.

This passage introduces a cornerstone of Hanafi mufti methodology: how to choose between conflicting rulings within the madhhab. The 'people of tarjih' have left us two types of guidance: explicit statements of preference (like 'sahih', 'asahh') and implicit signals from their consistent practice. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for issuing sound fatwas that align with the relied-upon positions of the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context of conflicting rulings
Recognize that when the statements of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad differ, or when narrations from them conflict, the mufti must turn to the 'people of tarjih' (later authorities who weighed evidences) for guidance.
This is the foundational scenario that triggers the need for tarjih.
2
Recognize explicit tarjih phrases
Learn the standard phrases used by Hanafi jurists to indicate explicit preference: 'هو الصحيح', 'هو الأصح', 'به يفتي', 'عليه الفتوى', 'هو المعتمد', and similar expressions.
These phrases have a recognized hierarchy that will be detailed in a later principle.
3
Detect implicit tarjih from author's practice
Understand that when no explicit phrase is used, the consistent practice (صنيع) of a respected author or mufti can indicate an implicit preference. For example, always citing one ruling first or building upon it in subsequent discussion.
Implicit tarjih is a valid form of preference but is subordinate to explicit tarjih.
4
Apply the hierarchy: explicit over implicit
When both types are found on the same issue, the explicit tarjih must be followed. If only implicit exists, it is authoritative. The passage explicitly states: 'where explicit is found, it takes precedence over the implicit'.
This rule prevents the mufti from mistakenly favouring an inferred preference when a clear statement exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل السادس الترجيح من أصحاب الترجيح قد يكون صريحاً وقد يكون التزاماً، فحيث لم يوجد الترجيحُ الصّريح عُمِل بالترجيح الالتزامي، وحيثُ وُجد التصريح فهو مقدم على الالتزام. قد ذكرنا فيما سبق أنه إذا اختلفت أقوال أصحاب المذهب، أو اختلفت الروايات عنهم، فيؤخذ منها ما رجّحه أصحاب الترجيح. والترجيح المروي عنهم على قسمين: صريح والتزامي. أما الصريح، فما كان بألفاظ هي صريحة في الترجيح، كقولهم "هو الصحيح " و "هو الأصح" و "به يُفتي" و "عليه الفتوى" و "هو المعتمد " وأشباه ذلك. وسيأتي بيان مراتب هذه الألفاظ في الأصل الآتى إن شاء الله تعالى. وأما الترجيح الالتزامي، فما لم يكن بألفاظ صريحة، وإنما دلّ عليه صنيع المؤلّف أو المفتى المعروف بذلك الصنيع. وله صُور مختلفة:
The sixth principle: Tarjih (preference) from the people of tarjih is sometimes explicit and sometimes implicit. Where explicit tarjih is not found, implicit tarjih is acted upon, and where explicit is found, it takes precedence over the implicit. We have mentioned previously that when the statements of the scholars of the madhhab differ, or the narrations from them differ, then what is preferred by the people of tarjih is taken. Tarjih transmitted from them is of two types: explicit and implicit. As for explicit, it is that which uses words that are explicit in preference, such as their saying 'it is sahih', 'it is asahh', 'by it fatwa is given', 'on it the fatwa relies', 'it is the relied-upon', and the like. The explanation of the ranks of these expressions will come in the following principle, God willing. As for implicit tarjih, it is that which is not expressed with explicit words, but rather is indicated by the practice of the author or mufti known for that practice. And it has various forms:
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of tarjih (preference) in the Hanafi madhhab. When there are conflicting rulings from the founders (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) or conflicting narrations, the mufti must adopt the position that the 'people of tarjih' (later authorities who weighed evidences) have preferred. Their preference can be explicit (e.g., using phrases like 'the correct view is...' or 'the fatwa is upon...') or implicit (inferred from the author's consistent practice, such as always citing one ruling first or building upon it). The author promises to elaborate on the hierarchy of explicit tarjih phrases later. The lesson teaches the mufti to recognize both types and prioritize explicit over implicit.

Key Terms
الترجيح الصريح (al-tarjih al-sarih): Explicit preference indicated by clear terms like 'sahih', 'asahh', 'upon it is the fatwa', etc.
الترجيح الالتزامي (al-tarjih al-iltizami): Implicit preference inferred from the author's consistent practice or methodology.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a mufti finds both an explicit tarjih and an implicit tarjih on the same issue, which should he follow?
A) The implicit tarjih because it is from the author's practice.
B) The explicit tarjih because it takes precedence over the implicit.
C) He must look for another source.
D) He should follow the majority of scholars regardless.

Key Takeaway
Explicit tarjih words (sahih, asahh, etc.) always outweigh implicit tarjih (author's practice) when both are present.

Explicit and Implicit Preponderance in Fatwa
Explains the sixth principle: tarjih types and five forms of implicit tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish explicit from implicit tarjih and identify the five forms of implicit tarjih based on authorial practice.

Core Idea
When no explicit tarjih exists, the mufti must infer the stronger opinion from the author's consistent practice.

In this lesson, we explore the sixth principle of Hanafi fatwa methodology: the classification of tarjih into explicit (ṣarīḥ) and implicit (iltizāmī). While explicit terms like 'ṣaḥīḥ' or 'alayhi al-fatwa' are clear indicators, often the works of the madhhab do not use such terms. Instead, the mufti must discern the preponderant view from the author's method—how he orders opinions, presents evidence, or even what he omits. The passage enumerates five concrete forms of such implicit tarjih, giving the student a practical toolkit for navigating Hanafi texts.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish explicit from implicit tarjih
Understand that explicit tarjih uses direct phrases like 'ṣaḥīḥ', while implicit tarjih is deduced from the author's methodology. Explicit takes precedence over implicit.
2
Identify the first form: order of mention
Some authors (like Qadi Khan) mention the preponderant opinion first, indicating its weight. This is a known convention.
Qadi Khan explicitly states this practice in his Fatawa.
3
Identify the second form: evidence placement
In books like al-Hidayah, the evidence for the preponderant opinion is mentioned last, after refuting others. The last evidence signals the rājiḥ view.
This is the most common form in didactic texts.
4
Identify the third and fourth forms: evidence mention and refutation patterns
Mentioning evidence for only one opinion implies its strength; refuting evidence for some but not others indicates the unrefuted opinion is preferred.
Both are implicit signals that require careful reading.
5
Identify the fifth form: inclusion in authoritative texts
Mere appearance in a reliable matn (like al-Mukhtar) suffices to indicate the opinion's being rājiḥ. These texts are benchmarks of the school.
The mutun mu'tabara are considered authoritative sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل السادس
الترجيح من أصحاب الترجيح قد يكون صريحاً وقد يكون التزاماً، فحيث لم يوجد الترجيحُ الصّريح عُمِل بالترجيح الالتزامي، وحيثُ وُجد التصريح فهو مقدم على الالتزام.
قد ذكرنا فيما سبق أنه إذا اختلفت أقوال أصحاب المذهب، أو اختلفت الروايات عنهم، فيؤخذ منها ما رجّحه أصحاب الترجيح. والترجيح المروي عنهم على قسمين: صريح والتزامي.
أما الصريح، فما كان بألفاظ هي صريحة في الترجيح، كقولهم "هو الصحيح " و "هو الأصح" و "به يُفتي" و "عليه الفتوى" و "هو المعتمد " وأشباه ذلك. وسيأتي بيان مراتب هذه الألفاظ في الأصل الآتي إن شاء الله تعالى.
وأما الترجيح الالتزامي، فما لم يكن بألفاظ صريحة، وإنما دلّ عليه صنيع المؤلّف أو المفتى المعروف بذلك الصنيع. وله صُور مختلفة:
الصورة الأولى: تقديم القول الراجح. فقد التزم بعض المؤلفين بأنّهم يذكرون القول الراجح عندهم قبل ذكر الأقوال المرجوحة، وهذا هو دأب قاضي خان رحمه الله تعالى في فتاواه، لأنّه قال في أوّل الفتاوى: "و فيما كثرت فيه الأقاويل من المتأخرين، اقتصرت على قول أو قولين، وقدمت ما هو الأظهر، وافتتحت بما هو الأشهر، إجابة للطالبين وتيسيراً على الراغبين". وكذلك صاحب "ملتقى الأبحر" التزم تقديم القول المعتمد على غيره من الأقوال. ويظهر من صنيع صاحب البدائع أنه يفعل ذلك أيضاً في الغالب.
الصورة الثانية: تأخير دليل القول الراجح، فإن الكتب التي التزمت ذكرَ الدلائل كالهداية، والمبسوط وغيرهما، فإنّ عادتهم المعروفة أنهم يذكرون دليل القول الراجح في الأخير، و يُجيبون عن دلائل أقوال أخر، فالدليل المذكور أخيراً يدل على رجحان مدلوله عند المؤلف.
الصورة الثالثة: ذكر دليل القول الراجح. وهذا إذا ذكر دليل قولٍ واحدٍ فقط، و أهْمِل دليل الآخر. فالراجح ما ذكر دليله.
الصورة الرابعة: الردُّ على الأقوال الأخر، وهذا إذا ذَكَرَ فقيه أقوالاً مع دلائلها، ثم رد على دلائل بعض الأقوال، ولم يرد على دليل بعضها، فذلك ترجيح التزامي لقول لم يرد على دليله.
الصورة الخامسة: أن يكون القول مذكوراً في المتون المعتبرة، فإن ذكرها في تلك المتون يكفي بمجرده للدلالة على أنه هو الراجح في المذهب.
The Sixth Principle: Preponderance (tarjih) from those qualified to give preponderance may be explicit or implicit. So where explicit preponderance is not found, implicit preponderance is acted upon; and where explicit [preponderance] is found, it takes precedence over the implicit. We have mentioned previously that when the statements of the school's founders differ, or the narrations from them differ, what is taken is what the people of tarjih have given preponderance to. The preponderance reported from them is of two types: explicit and implicit. As for explicit, it is that which uses words that are explicit in indicating preponderance, such as their saying 'it is sahih', 'it is asahh', 'by it fatwa is given', 'upon it is fatwa', 'it is mu'tamad', and the like. The explanation of the ranks of these expressions will come in the next principle, God willing. As for implicit preponderance, it is that which is not in explicit words, but is indicated by the practice of the author or mufti known for that practice. It has various forms: The first form: Mentioning the preponderant opinion first. For some authors commit to mentioning the preponderant opinion before the weak opinions. This is the way of Qadi Khan (may God have mercy on him) in his Fatawa, for he said at the beginning of the Fatawa: 'In matters that have many opinions among the later scholars, I have limited [myself] to one or two opinions, and I have presented what is most evident, and begun with what is most famous, in response to seekers and for ease of those who desire [knowledge]. Similarly, the author of Multaqa al-Abhar committed to presenting the relied-upon opinion over other opinions. And it appears from the practice of the author of al-Bada'i' that he also does that most often. The second form: Delaying the evidence for the preponderant opinion. For books that commit to mentioning evidences, such as al-Hidaya, al-Mabsut, and others, their known custom is that they mention the evidence for the preponderant opinion last, and they respond to the evidences of other opinions. So the evidence mentioned last indicates the preponderance of its implication according to the author. The third form: Mentioning the evidence for the preponderant opinion. This is when the evidence for only one opinion is mentioned, and the evidence for the other is omitted. So the preponderant is that whose evidence is mentioned. The fourth form: Refuting the other opinions. This is when a jurist mentions opinions along with their evidences, then refutes the evidences of some opinions, but does not refute the evidence of some. That is an implicit preponderance for the opinion whose evidence was not refuted. The fifth form: That the opinion is mentioned in the authoritative primary texts (mutun mu'tabara). For its mention in those texts alone suffices to indicate that it is the preponderant opinion in the school.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti ruling from 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, presenting the sixth principle: the classification of tarjih (legal preponderance) into explicit and implicit. The author, Mufti Muhammad Taqi Usmani, explains that when there is no explicit statement of which opinion is preferred (e.g., 'this is sahih', 'the fatwa is upon this'), the mufti must infer the preponderant position from the consistent practice of the reliable authors and muftis in the school. He then enumerates five forms of such implicit tarjih: (1) the author's habit of mentioning the preponderant opinion first—citing Qadi Khan's Fatawa and the Multaqa al-Abhar; (2) the practice in books like al-Hidaya of placing the evidence for the preponderant opinion last after refuting opposing evidences; (3) mentioning evidence for only one opinion, thereby indicating its weight; (4) refuting the evidence of some opinions while leaving others untouched, the unchecked one being preferred; and (5) mere inclusion of an opinion in the authoritative mutun (e.g., al-Mukhtar, al-Kanz, al-Wiqaya), which signals its reliability. The passage underscores the Hanafi method of using authorial practice (san'i) as a source of tarjih when explicit labels are absent.

Key Terms
الترجيح (al-tarjīḥ): The process of determining which legal opinion is stronger (rājiḥ) and therefore binding for fatwa when multiple opinions exist within the madhhab.
الترجيح الصريح (al-tarjīḥ al-ṣarīḥ): Explicit tarjih using clear terminology such as 'sahih', 'asahh', 'by it fatwa is given', 'upon it is fatwa', 'mu'tamad'.
الترجيح الالتزامي (al-tarjīḥ al-iltizāmī): Implicit tarjih deduced from the consistent practice (san'i) of authors or muftis, e.g., ordering of opinions, evidence presentation, or omission of refutation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the sixth principle, if a Hanafi fiqh book consistently mentions the evidence for the preponderant opinion last, what does this indicate?
A) That the author is uncertain about which opinion is correct.
B) That the opinion whose evidence is mentioned last is the preponderant one according to the author.
C) That both opinions are equally weak.
D) That the earlier evidence is always for the preferred opinion.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fatwa methodology, when explicit tarjih is absent, the mufti must infer the preponderant opinion from the author's consistent practice, such as ordering of opinions and evidence presentation.

Five Methods of Identifying the Preferred Opinion in Hanafi Texts
Five methods of indicating the preferred opinion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the five authorial conventions used in Hanafi fiqh works to determine the preferred opinion (al-qawl al-rajih) for fatwa.

Core Idea
Five textual clues reveal the rajih: order, proof placement, exclusive proof, selective refutation, and matn authority.

When consulting classical Hanafi works, a mufti faces multiple opinions. Scholars developed conventions to signal which view is relied upon. This lesson unpacks five forms that systematically guide you to the mufta bihi position. Mastering these is essential for effective fatwa derivation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five forms
List each form with its distinguishing feature as described in the passage.
Forms are sequential: ordering, proof arrangement, exclusive proof, selective refutation, and matn authority.
2
Connect each form to its legal logic
For each form, explain why it indicates preference—e.g., delaying proof signals the author's final position.
The logic often follows pedagogical or dialectical patterns.
3
Distinguish implicit vs explicit correction
Differentiate the fifth form's tas-hih iltizami (implicit correction via matn) from tas-hih sarih (explicit correction by later scholars).
Explicit correction overrides implicit correction.
4
Apply to a sample text
Given a passage from a Hanafi work, determine which form is being used to signal the rajih.
Practice identifying forms in actual texts.
5
Evaluate the hierarchy
Understand that explicit correction (tas-hih sarih) overrides implicit correction (matn), and the five forms serve as indicators within that hierarchy.
The example of marriage without a guardian illustrates this hierarchy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تلخيص قواعد رسم المفتي
الصورة الأولى: تقديم القول الراجح. فقد التزم بعض المؤلفين بأنّهم يذكرون القول الراجح عندهم قبل ذكر الأقوال المرجوحة، وهذا هو دأب قاضي خان رحمه الله تعالى في فتاواه، لأنّه قال في أوّل الفتاوى: "و فيما كثرت فيه الأقاويل من المتأخرين، اقتصرت علي قول أو قولين، وقدمت ما هو (1) الأظهر، وافتتحت بما هو الأشهر، إجابة للطالبين وتيسيراً علي الراغبين . وكذلك صاحب "ملتقي الأبحر " التزم تقديم القول المعتمد علي غيره من الأقوال و يظهر من صنيع صاحب البدائع أنه يفعل ذلك أيضاً في الغالب. الصورة الثانية: تأخير دليل القول الراجح، فإن الكتب التي التزمت ذكرَ الدلائل كالهداية، والمبسوط وغيرهما، فإنّ عادتهم المعروفة أنهم يذكرون دليل القول الراجح فى الأخير، و يُجيبون عن دلائل أقوال أخر، فالدليل المذكور أخيراً يدل علي رجحان مدلوله عند المؤلف. الصورة الثالثة: ذكر دليل القول الراجح. وهذا إذا ذكر دليل قولٍ واحدٍ فقط، و أهْمِل دليل الآخر. فالراجح ما ذكر دليله.
الصورة الرابعة: الردُّ على الأقوال الأخر، وهذا إذا ذَكَرَ فقية أقوالاً مع دلائلها، ثم رد على دلائل بعض الأقوال، ولم يرد على دليل بعضها، فذلك ترجيح التزامي لقول لم يرد على دليله.
الصورة الخامسة: أن يكون القول مذكوراً فى المتون المعتبرة، فإن ذكرها فى تلك المتون يكفى بمجرده للدلالة على أنه هو الراجح في المذهب وإن لم تكن فيها صراحة بترجيحه، وذلك لأن المتونَ إنَّما وضعت لبيان الراجح من المذهب والمتون المعتبرة هى البداية، ومختصر القدوري والمختار ، والنُّقاية، والوقاية، والكنز، والملتقى، كما ذكره ابن عابدین رحمه الله تعالى في شرح عقود رسم المفتى وذكر عن العلامة قاسم (1) رحمه الله تعالى أنه قال: "مافي المتون مصحح تصحيحاً التزاميّاً." وذكر مثله عن عدةٍ من المشايخ كما ذكر عنهم أنّ التصحيح الصريخ مقدم على الالتزامي، فلو صحح المشايخ من أصحاب الترجيح قولاً مخالفاً لما فى المتون، فإنّه هو الراجح (2) ومثاله ماذكر فى المتون أن النكاح بغير ولي ينعقد في غير كفؤ، إلا أن الولي له حق الاعتراض ولكن رجّح المشايخ رواية الحسن بن زياد رحمه الله تعالى أنه لا ينعقد أصلاً.
Summary of the Rules of the Office of Mufti
First Form: Presenting the preferred opinion. Some authors commit to mentioning the preferred opinion before mentioning the less preferred opinions. This is the practice of Qadi Khan, may Allah have mercy on him, in his Fatawa, because he said at the beginning of al-Fatawa: 'Regarding what has many statements from the later scholars, I limited myself to one or two statements, and I presented what is most apparent, and I opened with what is most well-known, responding to seekers and making it easy for those who desire.' Likewise, the author of Multaqa al-Abhur committed to presenting the relied-upon opinion over other opinions, and it appears from the practice of the author of al-Bada'i' that he also does this generally. Second Form: Delaying the evidence for the preferred opinion. For books that commit to mentioning proofs, like al-Hidayah, al-Mabsut, and others, their known habit is that they mention the proof for the preferred opinion at the end, and they respond to the proofs of other opinions. So the proof mentioned last indicates the preference of its implication according to the author. Third Form: Mentioning the proof of the preferred opinion. This is when only the proof of one opinion is mentioned, and the proof of the other is omitted. So the preferred is that whose proof is mentioned. Fourth Form: Refuting other opinions. This is when a jurist mentions opinions with their proofs, then refutes the proofs of some opinions and does not refute the proof of some others. So that is an implicit preference for the opinion whose proof was not refuted. Fifth Form: That the opinion is mentioned in the reliable matn texts. Indeed, its mention in those matn texts alone suffices to indicate that it is the preferred opinion in the school, even if there is no explicit preference in them. This is because the matn texts were only authored to state the preferred view of the school. The reliable matn texts are al-Bidayah, Mukhtasar al-Quduri, al-Mukhtar, al-Nuqayah, al-Wiqayah, al-Kanz, and al-Multaqa, as mentioned by Ibn Abidin, may Allah have mercy on him, in Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. He mentioned from 'Allamah Qasim, may Allah have mercy on him, that he said: 'What is in the matn texts is an implicit correction.' And he mentioned similarly from several shuyukh, as he mentioned from them that explicit correction takes precedence over implicit correction. So if the shuyukh who are among the people of tarjih correct a statement contrary to what is in the matn texts, then it is the preferred opinion. An example of that is what is mentioned in the matn texts: that marriage without a guardian is valid in the case of a non-compatible match, except that the guardian has the right of objection. But the shuyukh preferred the transmission of al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, may Allah have mercy on him, that it is not valid at all.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage presents five forms (صور) used by Hanafi authors to signal which opinion is the preferred (rajih) one within the madhhab. These are not substantive rules of fiqh but methodological tools for the mufti to identify the mufta bihi view when consulting classical works.

The first form is explicit ordering: the author places the preferred opinion first. Qadi Khan and the author of Multaqa al-Abhur are cited as examples.

The second form is the arrangement of proofs: in works like al-Hidayah and al-Mabsut, the proof for the rajih opinion is given last. Since the author systematically answers objections to it and leaves it last, it indicates his preference.

The third form is exclusive mention of proof: if only one opinion's evidence is given and others are ignored, that opinion is likely the preferred one.

The fourth form is selective refutation: if an author discusses several opinions with their proofs but only refutes some, the unrefuted one is implicitly preferred.

The fifth form concerns the authoritative matn texts (al-Mutan al-Mu'tabara). These texts—listed as al-Bidayah, Mukhtasar al-Quduri, al-Mukhtar, al-Nuqayah, al-Wiqayah, al-Kanz, and al-Multaqa—are composed to state the correct position of the madhhab. An opinion found in any of these is presumed correct by implicit correction (tas-hih iltizami). However, explicit correction (tas-hih sarih) by later tarjih scholars overrides the matn's implication. The example given is marriage without a guardian: the matn says it is valid but the guardian may object, while later scholars preferred the riwayah of Hasan ibn Ziyad that it is invalid entirely.

This lesson is crucial for a mufti to understand how to navigate the Hanafi textual tradition, recognizing the difference between implicit and explicit correction and the relative authority of texts.

Key Terms
القول الراجح (al-qawl al-rajih): The opinion that is preferred and relied upon for fatwa within the Hanafi school, identified through authorial conventions or direct tarjih.
المتون المعتبرة (al-mutun al-mu'tabara): The reliable matn texts in the Hanafi school that are intended to convey the preferred view. The listed texts include al-Bidayah, Mukhtasar al-Quduri, al-Mukhtar, al-Nuqayah, al-Wiqayah, al-Kanz, and al-Multaqa.
التصحيح الصريخ (al-tas-hih al-sarih): Explicit correction: when later authorities clearly state that a particular opinion is the correct one, even if it contradicts the matn.
التصحيح الالتزامي (al-tas-hih al-iltizami): Implicit correction: the presumption that any ruling found in the reliable matn texts is the correct position of the madhhab, without an explicit statement to that effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT listed among the reliable matn texts (المتون المعتبرة) that carry implicit correction?
A) البداية
B) الهداية
C) الكنز
D) الملتقى

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufti must master five textual conventions and the hierarchy of implicit vs explicit correction to correctly identify the mufta bihi position.

Authority of Mutun and Explicit Tarjih
Explaining the authoritative status of mutun and the precedence of explicit tarjih over implicit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of explicit tarjih over implicit authentication of the mutun to determine the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Explicit tarjih by later scholars overrides the implicit authority of the mutun.

In the Hanafi madhhab, the mutun (core texts) are considered repositories of the relied-upon rulings. However, later scholars may explicitly correct a ruling found in the mutun. This passage establishes the hierarchy: explicit correction (tas'hih sarih) takes precedence over the implicit authentication (tas'hih iltizami) of the mutun. Understanding this rule is crucial for a mufti when determining the operative fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of correction
The passage distinguishes between implicit correction (tas'hih iltizami) of the mutun and explicit correction (tas'hih sarih) by later scholars.
2
Understand the hierarchy
Explicit correction takes precedence over implicit. The phrase 'التصحيح الصريح مقدم على الالتزامي' is key.
3
Apply to the example
Marriage without guardian: mutun say valid, later scholars said invalid. The explicit correction wins.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
For fatwa, follow the explicitly corrected view, not the mutun.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن لم تكن فيها صراحة بترجيحه، وذلك لأن المتونَ إنَّما وضعت لبيان الراجح من المذهب والمتون المعتبرة هى البداية، ومختصر القدوري والمختار ، والنُّقاية، والوقاية، والكنز، والملتقى، كما ذكره ابن عابدین رحمه الله تعالى في شرح عقود رسم المفتى وذكر عن العلامة قاسم ) رحمه الله تعالى أنه قال: "مافي المتون مصحح تصحيحاً التزاميّاً." وذكر مثله عن عدةٍ من المشايخ كما ذكر عنهم أنّ التصحيح الصريخ مقدم على الالتزامي، فلو صحح المشايخ من أصحاب الترجيح قولاً مخالفاً لما فى المتون، فإنّه هو الراجح ) ومثاله ماذكر فى المتون أن النكاح بغير ولي ينعقد في غير كفؤ، إلا أن الولي له حق الاعتراض ولكن رجّح المشايخ رواية الحسن بن زياد رحمه الله تعالى أنه لا ينعقد أصلاً ؟
And if there is no explicit expression giving it precedence, [the ruling in the mutun is still relied upon] because the mutun were composed to state the preferred view of the madhhab. The authoritative mutun are: al-Bidaya, Mukhtasar al-Quduri, al-Mukhtar, al-Nuqaya, al-Wiqaya, al-Kanz, and al-Multaqa, as mentioned by Ibn Abidin in Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. He also related from 'Allama Qasim that he said: 'What is in the mutun has been authentically established with implicit correction.' And he mentioned similar from several mashayikh, as they reported from them that explicit correction takes precedence over implicit correction. So if the scholars who are capable of tarjih explicitly correct a view contrary to that found in the mutun, then that is the preferred view. An example is what is mentioned in the mutun: that marriage without a guardian is valid (in the case of a non-competent [woman?]), except that the guardian has the right to object, but the mashayikh preferred the narration of al-Hasan ibn Ziyad that it is not valid at all.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage states a methodological rule for muftis. The foundational texts (mutun) of the Hanafi school are assumed to contain the most correct rulings, as they were compiled with implicit authentication. However, if later scholars specifically and explicitly correct a ruling from the mutun, that explicit correction takes precedence and becomes the relied-upon position. The example given is marriage without a guardian: the mutun say it is valid but with the guardian's right to object, but the later scholars preferred the anomalous narration of Hasan ibn Ziyad that it is not valid at all. This shows that explicit tarjih overrides the implicit endorsement in the mutun.

Key Terms
المتون (al-mutun): The core authoritative texts of the Hanafi madhhab that contain the relied-upon rulings.
تصحيح التزامي (tas'hih al-iltizami): Implicit authentication: the inclusion of a ruling in the mutun indicates it is correct without explicit statement.
تصحيح صريح (tas'hih sarih): Explicit correction: later scholars directly stating that a different ruling is correct, overriding the mutun.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The explicit correction by later scholars

Key Takeaway
Explicit corrections (tas'hih sarih) by later scholars override the implicit authority of the mutun.

Ranking of Tarjih Expressions in Hanafi Iftaa
Hierarchy of tarjih expressions and internal debate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the ranking of tarjih expressions in the Hanafi school and apply the correct one when conflicting phrases appear.

Core Idea
The hierarchy of tarjih phrases guides the mufti; 'practice of the ummah' is strongest, but 'sahih' and 'asahh' are debated.

In Hanafi fatwa practice, scholars use specific phrases to indicate which ruling is preferred. This lesson unpacks the ranking of these expressions, from the strongest ('upon it is the practice of the ummah') to weaker ones. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for a mufti when choosing between conflicting rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hierarchy of tarjih expressions
List the expressions in order of strength as given in the source: 'alayhi 'amalu al-ummah' > 'alayhi al-fatwa' / 'bihi yufta' > 'al-fatwa 'alayhi' > 'huwa al-sahih' > 'huwa al-asahh' > then 'al-mu'tamad' and 'al-ashbah' (superlative forms stronger).
Memorize the order: it is a core tool for fatwa preference.
2
Locate the debate on 'sahih' vs 'asahh'
Two opinions exist: some say 'asahh' is stronger due to superlative form; others say 'sahih' is stronger because its opposite is error. The passage presents both views.
This is an internal Hanafi ikhtilaf; both are used in texts.
3
Understand the resolution when the same scholar uses both
If the same scholar uses both terms, 'asahh' is stronger by consensus. But if different scholars, the dispute remains.
This practical rule resolves many apparent contradictions.
4
Identify the practical implication for a mufti
A mufti must weigh expressions carefully, considering the scholar's identity and context. The well-known view (according to Ibn 'Abidin) prefers 'asahh' over 'sahih'.
When in doubt, consult the later authorities like Ibn 'Abidin.
